2020.08.10 04.00 Bug fixes and correction to v03.00:

references
- Correcting YANG references for Non-Delay

- Correcting YANG references for enhanced U-Plane
markings
- Correcting YANG references in tables B.3 and C.3
- Clarify that validation of configuration is based on

specification
- Clarification of supervision

- Enabling static configuration of PRACH or SRS

and frequency errors

endpoint basis
- New optional feature – configurable full-scale
offset
- New optional feature - eAxC specific gain
correction
- New optional feature - TX gain reference level
control

access

definitions

Addition of new functionality, including:
- New NACM permissions for SMO and hybrid O-
DU
- New optional feature for performing
pnfRegistration
- New optional feature for configured YANG

- Bandwidth management to avoid over-subscription
of O-RU resources
- Shared cell with selective Tx/Rx using Beam ID
- Cascaded FHM Operation
- New capability to support co-ordinated (self)
antenna calibration

- Clarify operation of non-persistent M-Plane
- Clarify operation of Software Management

- Clarify eaxc-id assignment
- Clarify connectivity checks operation
- Clarify procedures for deleting configuration
- Clarify plug and play certificate aspects

Addition of new functionality, including:
- Optional support of NETCONF/TLS
- Supporting IPv6 only O-RUs

Chapter 1 Introductory Material 1
1.1 Scope 2
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN.org. 3
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN WG4 and may change following formal 4
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN.org modify the contents of the present document, it will be re -released by O-RAN 5
Alliance with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows: 6
Release x.y.z 7
where: 8
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, i.e. technical enhancements, corrections, updates, etc. (the 9
initial approved document will have x=01). 10
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document. 11
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating incremental changes during the editing 12
process. 13
The present document specifies the management plane protocols used over the fronthaul interface linking the O-RU (O-RAN 14
Radio Unit) with other management plane entities, that may include the O-DU (O-RAN Distributed Unit), the O-RAN defined 15
Service Management and Orchestration (SMO) functionality as well as other generic Network Management Systems (NMS).  16
1.2 References 17
The following documents contain provisions which, through reference in this text, constitute provisions of the present document. 18
- References are either specific (identified by date of publication, edition number, version number, etc.) or non-specific. 19
- For a specific reference, subsequent revisions do not apply. 20
- For a non-specific reference, the latest version applies. In the case of a reference to a 3GPP document (including a GSM 21
document), a non-specific reference implicitly refers to the latest version of that document in Release 15. 22

Working Group 4  25

1.3 Definitions and Abbreviations 9
1.3.1 Definitions 10
For the purposes of the present document, the terms and definitions given in 3GPP TR 21.905 [1] and the following apply. A 11
term defined in the present document takes precedence over the definition of the same term, if any, in 3GPP TR 21.905 [1]. 12
Antenna Line: connection between O-RU and antenna 13
C-Plane: Control Plane: refers specifically to real-time control between O-DU and O-RU, and should not be confused with the 14
UE’s control plane 15
Cascade mode: Mode of Shared cell which is realized by several O-RUs cascaded in chain topology 16
DL: DownLink: data flow towards the radiating antenna (generally on the LLS interface) 17
eAxC: extended Antenna-Carrier: a data flow for a single antenna (or spatial stream) for a single carrier in a single sector. 18
Event-Collector: A REST server to which an O -RU supporting NON -PERSISTENT-NETCONF feature can send a JSON 19
notification 20
FHM mode: Mode of Shared cell which is realized by FHM and several O-RUs in star topology.  21
LLS: Lower Layer Split: logical interface between  O-DU and O-RU when using a  lower layer (intra-PHY based) functional 22
split. 23
LLS-U: Lower Layer Split User-plane: logical interface between O-DU and O-RU when using a lower layer functional split. 24
LLS-C: Lower Layer Split Control-plane: logical interface between O-DU and O-RU when using a lower layer functional split. 25
LLS-S: Lower Layer Split Synchro nization-plane: logical interface between O-DU and O-RU when using a lower layer 26
functional split. 27
High-PHY: those portions of the PHY processing on the O-DU side of the fronthaul interface, including FEC encode/decode, 28
scrambling, and modulation/demodulation. 29
Low-PHY: those portions of the PHY processing on the O-RU side of the fronthaul interface, including FFT/iFFT, digital 30
beamforming, and PRACH extraction and filtering. 31
M-Plane: Management Plane: refers to non-real-time management operations between the O-DU and the O-RU 32
North-node: the O-DU or a connected O-RU closer to the O-DU for the O-RU, e.g., the cascade O-RU#1 connected to O-33
RU#2 is north-node for O-RU#2, when O-DU, O-RU#1 and O-RU#2 are in cascade chain topology. The O-DU in star 34
topology connected to an FHM is north-node for the FHM.  35
NMS: A Network Management System dedicated to O-RU operations 36
Port: End of a transport link – in most cases this is an optical port 37
Port Number: A number which identifies a port (see Port). In case of SFP/SFP+ port, port number value is 0 to N -1 where N 38
is number of ports in the device. Numbers 0 to N-1 are assigned to ports in order following order of labels on the device (labels 39
for ports are not necessarily numbers starting from zero) 40
O-DU: O-RAN Distributed Unit: a logical node hosting PDCP/RLC/MAC/High-PHY layers based on a lower layer functional 41
split. 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          13
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
O-RU: O-RAN Radio Unit: a logical node hosting Low-PHY layer and RF processing based on a lower layer functional split.  1
This is similar to 3GPP’s “TRP” or “RRH” but more specific in including the Low-PHY layer (FFT/iFFT, PRACH extraction).   2
O-RU Controller: A network function that is permitted to control the configuration of an O-RU. Examples of O-RU controllers 3
include, an O-DU, a classical NMS, an O-RAN Service Management and Orchestration function, or other network automation 4
platforms.  5
S-Plane: Synchronization Plane: refers to traffic between the O-RU or O-DU to a synchronization controller which is generally 6
an IEEE-1588 Grand Master (however, Grand Master functionality may be embedded in the O-DU). 7
Shared cell: The operation for the same cell by several O-RUs.  8
Shared cell network: the network for several cascade O-RUs in a chain topology or the network for one FHM and several O-9
RUs in a star topology.  10
South-node: a connected O-RU far from O-DU for the O-RU, e.g., the cascade O-RU#2 connected to O-RU#1 is south-node 11
for O-RU#1, when O-DU, O-RU#1 and O-RU#2 are in cascade chain topology. The O-RU in star topology connected to an 12
FHM is south-node for the FHM. 13
Spatial stream: the data flow on the DL associated with precoded data (may be same as layers or different if there is expansion 14
in the precoding), and on UL associated with the number of outputs from the digital beamforming (sometimes called “beams”).  15
SSM: Synchronization Status Message: part of ITU G.781 and G.8264 standards. 16
TRX: Refers to the specific processing chain in an O-RU associated with D/A or A/D converters.  Due to digital beamforming 17
the number of TRXs may exceed the number of spatial streams, and due to analog beamforming the number of TRXs may be 18
lower than the number of antenna elements. 19
U-Plane: User Plane: refers to IQ sample data transferred between O-DU and O-RU 20
UL: Up-Link: data flow away from the radiating antenna (generally on the LLS interface) 21
Virtual Connection : a connection between O-RU and O-RU controller. This connection is established by means of 22
autodetection procedure and is supervised by supervision procedure. 23

1.4 Conventions 24
This management plane specification includes cross references to a set of associated YANG models. Text may reference 25
particular YANG leafs, notifications and remote procedure calls (RPCs). In order to assist in readability, all cross references to 26
YANG defined elements will keep the identical case format as defined in the corresponding YANG model, with the font-weight 27
set to bold. This convention applies only to text and not to YANG elements embedded into figures.  28
If there is any conflict between the YANG models and the accompanying text description in this specification, the definition of 29
the YANG models shall take precedence. 30

The revision statement in the YANG models will be used to describe future revisions t o the models that are backwards 1
compatible. Backwards incompatible changes will be addressed by incrementing the number used as part of the model name 2
and namespace, effectively creating a new YANG model. The format of the namespace used in all O-RAN YANG models is 3
“urn:o-ran:”<model-name>“:”<model-number>, where the initial <model -number> used in a newly defined YANG model is 4
“1.0”. Where this document makes reference to models, irre spective of their backward compatibi lity, a gen eric <model -5
number> of “x.y” is used to enable reference to all versions of the namespace for a particular <model-name>. 6

document where the corresponding description was introduced . For example, the reference in all revision statements for the 9
initial O-RAN models include cross-reference to “ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v01.00”.  10

model. All revision statement descriptions will begin with “version ” <a>“.”<b>“.”<c>, where <a>, <b> and <c> are used to 13
reflect the version of the YANG model, where 14

Chapter 2 High Level Description 22
2.1 Top level functional description, terminology, including hybrid, 23
hierarchical 24
2.1.1 Architecture for O-RAN WG4 Fronthaul functional split 25
This O-RAN FH specification addresses the lower layer functional split as depicted in Figure 1. Refer to the O-RAN CUS plane 26
specification [2] for more details on the split architecture. The Lower-Layer Split M-plane (LLS-M) facilitates the initialization, 27
configuration and management of the O-RU to support the stated functional split. 28
 29

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          16
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Figure 1 – O-RAN WG4 FH functional split 1
2.1.2 M-Plane architecture model 2
A NETCONF/YANG based M-Plane is used for supporting the management features including “start up” installation, software 3
management, configuration management, performance management, fault management and file management towards the O-4
RU. The M-Plane supports two architectural models: 5
1. Hierarchical model.  As shown on the left side Figure 1, the O-RU is managed entirely by one or more O-DU(s) using 6
a NETCONF based M-Plane interface. When the O-RU is managed by multiple O-DUs, it is typically for enabling O-DU 7
and/or transport connectivity redundancy capabilities. Refer to Chapter 3 for more details. 8
2. Hybrid model . As shown on the right side of Figure 1, the hybrid architecture enables one or more direct logical 9
interface(s) between management system (s) and O-RU in addition to a logical interface between O-DU and the O-RU. It 10
should be noted that the NETCONF clients connecting to the O-RU may be of different classes (e.g. O-DU and SMO). For 11
example, functions like O-RU software management, performance management, configuration management and fault 12
management can be managed directly by the management system(s).  13
In the hybrid model, the O-RU has end to end IP layer connectivity with the SMO. From a physical network point of view, this 14
connectivity could be via the O-DU, where the O-DU is acting as an IP/Ethernet packet forwarder, forwards the packets between 15
O-RU and the SMO. Direct logical communication between a n O-RU and SMO can be enabled via O-RUs being assigned 16
routable IPs or local private IPs resolved by a NAT function in the network (or implemented at the O-DU). Refer to chapter 3 17
for details how O-RU acquires the IP address of O-DU and SMO for the M-plane communication. 18
As described in Chapte r 3, there is no explicit signaling to indicate that an O-RU is operating in a hierarchical or hybrid 19
configuration. All NETCONF servers supporting this M -Plane specification shall support multiple NETCONF sessions, and 20
hence all complaint O-RUs shall be able to support both hierarchical and hybrid deployment. 21
 22
Figure 2 - M-Plane Architecture 23

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          17
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
NETCONF/YANG is used as the network element management protocol [3] and data modeling language [4]. Use of such a 1
standardized framework and common modeling language simplifies integration between O-DU and O-RU as well as operator 2
network integration (in terms of running service) in case of elements sharing a common set of capabilities . The framework 3
supports integration of products with differing capabilities enabled by well-defined published data models. NETCONF also 4
natively supports a hybrid architecture which enables multiple clients to subscribe and receive information originating at th e 5
NETCONF server in the O-RU. 6
2.1.3 Transport Network 7
Based on the transport topology, various modes of network connectivity are possible between O-RU and O-DU and SMO.  8
The basic requirement for M-Plane is to have end to end IP connectivity between the O-RU and the elements managing it (O-9
DU, SMO, or so called “O-RU Controllers”). The connectivity between the O-DU and SMO and its management plane are not 10
in scope of this specification. The O-RU shall support either IPv4 or IPv6 and optionally support dual stack (IPv4 and IPv6). 11
Note, in previous versions of this specification, only IPv4 was mandatory. In order to ensure backwards compatibility 12
with equipment supporting earlier versions of this specification, an operator and vendor can agree to use a common IP 13
version in the O-RU, O-DU and any other O-RU controllers. 14
2.1.4 M-Plane functional description 15
The M-Plane provides the following major functionalities to the O-RU. These features are implemented using the NETCONF 16
provided functions. 17
 “Start up” installation  18
During startup, the O-RU acquires its network layer parameters either via static (pre -configured in the O-RU) or dynamically 19
via DHCP or DHCPv6. During this process the O-RU may acquire the IP address of the O-RU controller(s), in which case the 20
O-RU establishes the NETCONF connectivity using the “call home” feature. When the O-RU is operating in an environment 21
which include the O-RAN defined SMO, the O-RU may acquire the IP address of t he event-collector(s), in which case the O-22
RU performs a pnfRegistration which triggers the SMO to establish NETCONF connectivity using the information recovered 23
from the pnfRegistration procedure.  The capability exchange is performed between the client an d server as part of the initial 24
NETCONF Hello exchanges. Details of these steps are provided in chapter 3. 25
Note, the use of “start up” terminology in this specification is distinct from the “startup” capability used in a NETCONF 26
environment to indicate that a device supports separate running and startup configuration datastores. This specification makes 27
specific reference to configuration which is required to be stored in “reset persistent memory”. The O-RU shall use this stored 28
configuration as its “startup” configuration. 29
SW management  30
The M-Plane is responsible for software download, installation, validation and activation of new SW when requested by O-RU 31
Controller. The software download is triggered by NETCONF RPC procedures, and the actual software package download is 32
done using sFTP. In this version of the M-Plane specification, sFTP is the only defined file transfer protocol for software and 33
file management. 34
Configuration management 35
Configuration management covers various scenarios like Retrieve Resource State, Modify Resource State, Modify Parameters 36
and Retrieve Parameters. NETCONF get-config and edit-config RPCs shall be used for configuration parameter retrieval and 37
updates at the O-RU  38
Performance management 39
Performance management describes the measurements and counters used to collect data related to O-RU operations. The 40
purpose of Performance Management is optimizing the operation of the O-RU.  41
The measurement results are reported by two options:  42
1. YANG Notification: This option uses the stats definition of YANG model per measurement group. In this case, get 43
rpc and/or notification will be used (see Chapter 7 for more details).  44

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          18
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
2. File Upload: This option uses the file upload procedure defined in File management. The measurement results are 1
saved to a data file periodically.  2
Fault Management 3
Fault management is responsible for sending alarm notif ications to the NETCONF Client. F ault Management allows alarm 4
notifications to be disabled or enabled as well as alarm subscription. 5
File Management 6
File management allows the O-RU Controller to trigger an O-RU to perform upload of files stored on O-RU to O-RU Controller. 7
The O-RU may provide different kinds of files and retrieved files can be used for various purposes. Simultaneous multiple file 8
upload operations can be supported under the same sFTP connection between O-RU to O-DU/SMO. 9
2.2 Interfaces 10
The M-Plane interface is defined between the O-RU Controller and the O-RU. The protocol stack of the M -Plane interface is 11
shown in Figure 3. The transport network layer is built on IP transport and SSH/TCP, and optionally TLS, is used to carry the 12
M-Plane message between the O-RU Controller and the O-RU. As an option, the O-RU may support the capability to support 13
asynchronous notifications to be sent using HTTPS. This option enables system optimization when the O-RU Controller  14
corresponds to the SMO which is operating with a non-persistent NETCONF session to the O-RU. 15
 16
Figure 3: M-plane protocol stack 17
2.3 YANG Module Introduction 18
The data models representing the M -Plane are organized as a set of reusable YANG modules. It is also the intent to reuse the 19
publicly available and generic YANG models as much as possible instead of developing customized O-RAN specific modules. 20
Refer to the various chapters, Annex D and the repository of YANG models for more details on each of these modules.  21
2.4 Security 22
The M-Plane provides end to end security as a mandatory feature, see Table 1. The M-Plane security shall be supported using 23
the SSHv2 layer in accordance with RFC 6242  [5]. TLS 1.2 in accordance with RFC 7589 [41] may be optionally supported . 24
TLS 1.3 in accordance with RFC 8446 [42] may also be optionally supported in addition to TLS 1.2.  RFC 6242 [5] and RFC 25
7589 [41] provide the procedure s for interoperability with NETCONF implementations. If there are multiple NETCONF 26
sessions established with a single O-RU, either SSH tunnels or TLS connections may be used and each session should be 27
established over a separate SSH tunnel  or TLS connection .  For the O -DU, the operator may use SSH, TLS, or both.  It is 28
recommended that operators use TLS in production networks. 29

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          19
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00

Table 1- M-Plane Security 1
SSHv2 may be used to perform SSH server host authentication, key exchange, encryption, and integrity protection. It also 2
derives a unique session ID that may be used by higher -level protocols. The end point (SSH client) authentication should be 3
done as per RFC 4252 [6]. Chapter 3 describes the authentication approach based on username and password  as well as based 4
on X.509 certificates. 5
The SSHv2 transport level security (encryption algorithms, data integrity algorithms) shall be based on RFC4253  [7]. As per 6
aes128-ctr shall be the mandatory ciphering protocol, and rest of the ones listed as optional. For data integrity, hmac-sha2-256 7
shall be the mandatory algorithm, and rest of the listed algorithms shall be optional. Public key-based host authentication shall 8
be used for authenticating the server (RFC 4253) by the clients, and username/password based client authentication shall be 9
done by the server as part of the SSH session establishment. The O-RU shall support the host key algorithms and key exchange 10
methods defined in section 10.1 of RFC 5656 for securing the Secure Shell (SSH) transport.   11
Note, in order to ensure backwards compatibility with equipment supporting earlier versions of this specification, an 12
operator and vendor may agree to use one of the optional ciphering protocols. 13
As an additional option, both client and server may implement authentication based on X.509 certificates. With this option, 14
RSA 2048 bit shall be supported for the Public Key algorithm, aes 128-ctr shall be supported for the cyphering algorithm and 15
hmac-sha2-256 shall be supported for integrity algorithm. 16
Note, the above specification will be replaced with a cross reference to t he O-RAN Security Task Group Guidelines 17
once such is published. 18
TLS 1.2 based on RFC 5246[38] performs mutual authentication, key exchange, encryption, and integrity protection to ensure 19
trusted communication between the NETCONF server (O-RU) and the NETCONF client (O-DU or SMO). NETCONF 20
implementations may support X.509 certificate based authentication using TLS 1.2 based on RFC 7589 [41]. When X.509 21
based authentication is used, NETCONF server identity is based on RFC 6125 [40] and NETCONF client identity is specified 22
in RFC 7589[41].  23
TLS 1.2 implementations shall support the following TLS Cipher Suites with SHA -256 and AES Galois Counter Mode in 24
accordance with RFC 7540 [42] and 3GPP TS 33.210 [46]: 25
• ECDHE_RSA_WITH_AES_128_GCM_SHA256 as defined in RFC 5289 [47]. 26
• DHE_RSA_WITH_AES_128_GCM_SHA256 as defined in RFC 5288 [48].   27
 28
It is mandatory  that TLS implementations follow t he rules on allowed cipher suites given in TLS 1.2 (RFC 5246) .  29
Implementations may include additional TLS cipher suites that provide mutual authentication and confidentiality as required 30
by NETCONF in RFC 6241 [3].  Only cipher suites with AEAD (e.g. GCM) and PFS (e.g. ECDHE, DHE) and recommended 31
by IANA [45] may be optionally supported.   . The disallowed cipher suites in RFC 7540 [49],  Appendix A, shall not be used.  32
The vendor and operator need to be prepared to replace integrity and/or ciphering algorithms if the current algorithm in use is 33
compromised or deprecated. TLS 1.2 shall follow TLS profiling defined in 3GPP TS 33.210 [46] section 6.2.3. 34
Operators may select the authentication mechanism and protocol to use as shown in Table 2. 35

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00

Chapter 3 “Start up” installation  2
This chapter provides the overall start-up mechanism from the power-on of O-RU to available in service. 3
Pre-condition:  4
- Power-ON for O-RU/NETCONF Server or O-RU restart operation.  5
 Power-ON for O-RU controller/NETCONF Client(s) and/or pnfRegistration event-collector. 6
- Physical interface(s) is(are) connected. 7
Post-condition:   8
- O-RU is ready for the radio transmission to the air on at least one carrier if packet transmission received from O-DU  9
- O-RU is ready for the packet transmission to the O-DU if radio reception received at the air on at least one carrier. 10
- At least one O-RU Controller/NETCONF client with either “super-user” or “hybrid-odu” access privileges can control the 11
carrier configuration of the O-RU/NETCONF server in O-RU. 12
 13

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          21
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 4: Overall of Start-Up Installation 2
 3

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          22
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
At the power-on of O-RU or following an O-RU restart, the following procedures are performed. 1
1. O-RU performs M-Plane transport layer resolution (DHCP, MAC, VLAN, IP, etc.) and recovers IP address(es) of O-RU 2
controller(s) and/or pnfRegistration event-collector. 3
2. O-RU begins synchronization of the O-RU against a Primary Reference Clock. (Note: step 2 may be in parallel with step 1 4
for some O-RU implementation.) 5
3. O-RU performs NETCONF Call Home to discovered O-RU controller(s) and/or performs pnfRegistr ation to discovered 6
event-collector. 7
4. O-RU controller performs SSH or TLS connection establishment. 8
5. O-RU and O-RU controller perform NETCONF capability discovery. 9
6. O-RU controller performs optional provisioning of new management accounts (typically only performed once during pre-10
staging) 11
7. O-RU and O-RU controller perform supervision of NETCONF connection. 12
8. O-RU controller performs retrieval of O-RU information. 13
9. O-RU controller performs SW management. 14
10. O-DU performs CU-Plane transport configuration 15
11. (opt) O-DU performs LBM configuration (CU-Plane over ETH) or enables UDP Echo (CU-Plane over IP). 16
12. (opt) O-DU performs initial C/U-Plane transport connectivity checking between O-DU and O-RU. 17
13. O-RU controller retrieves the O-RU delay profile from the O-RU. 18
14. O-RU controller performs U-Plane configuration between O-DU and O-RU. C/U-Plane transport connectivity between O-19
DU and O-RU is configured as part of this step. 20
15. O-DU optionally performs C/U-Plane delay measurements between O-DU and O-RU if the O-RU supports it. 21
16. O-RU controller performs Fault Management activation. 22
17. O-RU controller activates performance measurement (if required at start-up timing). 23
18. O-RU controller retrieves O-RU state, including synchronization information, from O-RU. 24
19. O-RU controller configures the O-RU operational parameters. 25
20. Service available. 26
Note, the synchronization procedures started in step 2 needs to be completed before service is available. 27
Note: periodic CU-Plane connectivity check is not considered as the part of start-up. Once configured in start-up phase, 28
CU-Plane connectivity check can later be performed periodically and at any time in run-time. 29
This chapter mainly covers 1 and 3 to 7 as sub-sections. 30

3.1 Management Plane Transport aspects 6
This sub-section provides the M-plane transport establishment scenario between O-RU and O-RU controller(s), such as O-DU 7
and/or SMO. The transport layer address of M -plane is only the target in this section. Transport aspects of the C plane and U 8
plane are covered in Chapter 4. 9
Pre-condition:  10
- Physical interface is connected. 11
- When operating in an environment using call -home, the NETCONF server and NETCONF Client(s) have an identical 12
NETCONF call home port configured, to ensure the NETCONF client listens on the same port used by the NETCONF Server. 13
Post-condition:   14
- Transport Layer address(es) for M-plane are known to O-RU and O-RU controllers.  15
- O-RU is aware of the physical port(s) for M-plane, e.g., if there are multiple ports in the O-RU. 16
- O-RU is aware of the VLAN(s) to be used for M-Plane, e.g., if VLANs are used in the transport network. 17
- Then O-RU is ready to establish TCP connection for NETCONF call home and/or for PNF registration. 18
For the transport establishment, there are the following alternatives: 19
a) Manual transport layer address configuration in O-RU. This configuration contains the addresses for O-RU and NETCONF 20
client(s) and/or the event-collector. The method to manually configure the O-RU is out of scope in this specification. Assuming 21
manual configuration is successful , the NETCONF server shall be able to  recover this configured information and use the o-22
ran-mplane-int.yang model to communicate this operational-state to a NETCONF client. 23
b) If IPv4 is supported, DHCP server provides O-RU’s transport layer address information together with the identity of the 24
NETCONF client and/or the identity of the event-collector. This identity encodes either the transport layer address or FQDN of 25
the NETCONF client or event-collector. If an FQDN is signaled, the O-RU shall use the DNS server address provided by the 26
DHCP server to recover the IP address corresponding to FQDN of the NETCONF client or event-collector. 27
c) If IPv6 is supported, Stateless Address Auto -Configuration (SLAAC) is used to configure the O-RU’s transport address 28
with the DHCPv6 server providing the identity of the NETCONF client and/or event-collector. This identity encodes either the 29
transport layer address or FQDN of the NETCONF client  or event-collector. If an FQDN is signaled, the O-RU shall use the 30
DNS server address provided by the DHCPv6 server to recover the IP address corresponding to FQDN of the NETCONF client 31
or event-collector.  32
Note, a NETCONF client can receive a hint as to  whether an O-RU supports a particular IP version by using the get rpc to 33
recover the list of interfaces supported by the O-RU and using the presence of the augmented ipv4 container or ipv6 container 34
in the o-ran-interfaces module as an indication that a particular IP version is supported. 35
The O-RU uses the o-ran-dhcp.yang model to be able to expose information signaled by the DHCP server. 36

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          24
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.

3.1.1 O-RU identification in DHCP 5
The O-RU shall identify itself to DHCP servers by using DHCP option(s) using the vendor-class-data string within the o-ran-6
dhcp YANG model. If the O-RU supports IPv4, there are two alternatives. One uses option 60 Vendor Class Identifier, RFC2132 7
[8]. The other uses option 124 Vendor Identifying Vendor Class Option , RFC3925 [9]. An O-RU implementing IPv4 shall 8
support at least one of these options. If the O-RU supports IPv6, then it shall identify itself using the DHCPv6 Vendor Class 9
Option. 10
DHCPv4 Vendor Class Option: 11
• Option: 60 12
• Vendor Class Identifier Option 60: string  13
The format of the vendor class string shall be configured to one of the following three options:  14
1. ““o-ran-ru2/<vendor>, e.g., “o-ran-ru2/vendorA” 15
2. “o-ran-ru2/<vendor>/<product-code>”, e.g., “o-ran-ru2/vendorA/ORUAA100” 16
3. “o-ran-ru2/<vendor>/<product-code>/<serial-number>”,e.g. , “o-ran-ru2/vendorA/ORUAA100/FR1918010111” 17
DHCPv4 Vendor-Identifying Vendor Class Option: 18
• Option: 124 19
• Enterprise number: O-RAN-alliance 53148 20
• Vendor-Class-Data: the format of the string shall follow the rules defined for the DHCPv4 Vendor Class Option 21
DHCPv6 Vendor Class Option: 22
• Option: 16 23
• Enterprise number: O-RAN-alliance 53148 24
• Vendor-Class-Data: the format of the string shall follow the rules defined for the DHCPv4 Vendor Class Option 25
The DHCP Server may use this information when allocating IP addresses or when configuring management plane O-RU 26
Controller(s) information in the O-RU. 27
3.1.2 Management Plane VLAN Discovery Aspects 28
The O-RU will be connected to one or more Ethernet p orts. The transport systems may be realized such that these Ethernet 29
ports may be configured either as an access port, where untagged Ethernet frames are used, or as a trunk port, where multiple 30
VLANs are configured. At start up, the O-RU will typically not be able to immediately determine whether its ports are attached 31
to remote transport equipment configured for access or trunk mode operation.   32
Once an O-RU completes its boot-up sequence and Ethernet connectivity is detected on at least one of its Ethern et interfaces, 33
the O-RU starts management plane connection establishment. 34
The O-RU needs to determine whether it is connected to an access port or a trunk port. In particular, when connected to a trunk 35
port, the O-RU needs to additionally determine the VLAN identity/ies used to support the management plane communication(s). 36
The VLAN(s) used to support management plane communications can be identified by the DHCP server replying to the DHCP 37
DISCOVER message, as described in sections 3.1.4 and 3.1.6. 38

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          26
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Note, an O-RU which supports IPv6 may infer that a VLAN is not used to support management plane communications if it 1
receives an IPv6 Router Advertisement without either the “managed address configuration” or “other configuration” bits set. 2
An O-RU may have been p reviously configured with management plane VLAN information, for example storing the last 3
VLAN(s) used for management plane connectivity, and/or being previously configured with a range of management plane 4
VLANs by a NETCONF client that has been stored in reset-persistent memory. The O-RU may use this information to optimize 5
its discovery of the VLAN ID(s) used for management plane connectivity. 6
If the O-RU does not have previously configured management plane VLAN information, the O-RU shall attempt to discover 7
DHCP servers on all of its Ethernet ports using untagged Ethernet frames.  8
If the O-RU does not receive a DHCP OFFER from a DHCP server using untagged frames, or previously configured VLANs, 9
the O-RU should attempt to contact a DHCP server using individual VLANs on all of its Ethernet ports. 10
3.1.3 O-RU Management Plane IP Address Assignment 11
Automatic IP address assignment for the O-RU management plane can be achieved using different techniques: 12
1. IPv4 configuration using DHCPv4, RFC2131 [10] enables DHCP servers to configure IPv4 network address(es) on the O-13
RU. An O-RU implementing IPv4 shall support the behavior specified in RFC 4361 [33], using stable DHCPv4 node identifiers 14
in their dhcp-client-identifier option. 15
Note: a network realized with multiple DHCP servers should ensure that their configurations are coordinated to ensure a 16
common default gateway is provisioned in an O -RU which receives multiple DHCPv4 responses, e.g., when received over 17
different interfaces. 18
Note: an O-RU may indicate that it supports configuration of routing information using RFC 3442, enabling static routes to be 19
used by the O-RU when determining how to route uplink packets, e.g., when the O-RU supports multiple interfaces. 20
For O-RUs that support IPv6, both stateful and stateless address assignment procedures are supported: 21
2. IPv6 Stateless Address Auto-Configuration (SLAAC), RFC4862 [11] enables the O-RU to generate link-local and global 22
addresses. 23
Note: a network realized with multiple IPv6-enabled routers that support dynamic address assignment is expected to use RFC 24
4191 to configure the preference of the default route prefixes learnt by the O-RU using SLAAC. 25
3. IPv6 State-full address configuration uses DHCPv6 , RFC3315 [12] and enables DHCP servers to configure IPv6 network 26
address(es) on the O-RU. DHCPv6 is transported using UDP, using the  link-local address on the O-RU and a link -scoped 27
multicast address on the DHCP server.  28
Note: the above does not restrict the realization of the DHCP server, which may be integrated with the O-DU, may be provided 29
by the transport system, or may be accessed via a relay. 30
The DHCP server should operate using static bindings, i.e., ensuring an O-RU identified by a particular client hardware address 31
will be re-allocated the same management plane IP address, e.g., after performing an O-RU reset procedure. 32
3.1.4 O-RU Controller Discovery 33
This section provides how to automatically discover the O-RU Controller address(es). 34
O-RUs that have obtained their IPv6 addresses by stateless address auto -configuration, shall use stateless DHCPv6, RFC3736 35
[13], to obtain management plane configuration information.  36
Other O-RUs operating using stateful IPv4 or IPv6 address allocations shall obtain management plane configuration information 37
during IP address allocation. 38
The O-RU as NETCONF Server shall be able to recover NETCONF Client information using the following DHCP Options , 39
RFC8572 [14]:  40
• DHCPv4 OPTION V4_SZTP_REDIRECT [143] 41
• DHCPv6 OPTION_V6_SZTP_REDIRECT [136] 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          27
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
These options are defined in [ 14] and are used to deliver bootstrap -server-list information to the O-RU. The O-RU shall use 1
these options to recover the NETCONF client information using the above I ANA defined DHCP options. The O-RU is not 2
required to implement the remainder of the zerotouch capabilities defined in [14].  3
The above DHCP option provided information is encoded as a list of one or more server URIs, of the format “https://<ip -4
address-or-hostname>[:<port>]” signaled to the O-RU. The DHCP server shall ensure that all NETCONF client information is 5
encoded with these options, including the optional port information using the IANA assigned ports specified in RFC8071 [15]. 6
The O-RU shall use the included port information to decide whether to call home using NETCONF/SSH or NETCONF/TLS. 7
If no call home port is provided, the O-RU shall attempt to call home using NETCONF/SSH. 8
Other O-RUs which have had their IP address(es) manually configured, shall also have their O-RU Controller(s) manually 9
configured. 10
For IPv4, the O-RU may request the OPTION_V4_SZTP_REDIRECT by including its option code in the Parameter Request 11
List (55) in DHCP discover/request messages. 12
For IPv6, the O-RU may request the OPTION_V6_SZTP_REDIRECT option by including the requested option codes in the 13
Option Request Option. 14
Note, these operations are optional because the DHCP server will already be aware that it is communicating with an O-RU 15
based on the recovered vendor class option. 16
To enable O-RUs to operate in legacy environments where the DHCP server has not been enhanced with IANA defined DHCP 17
options for zero touch NETCONF capability, an O-RAN defined vendor specific option can be used to signal all NETCONF 18
client information to the O-RU using option 43 for DHCPv4 and option 17 for DHCPv6.  Multiple instances of NETCONF 19
client information may be signaled, encoded as a sequence of type/length/value fields. 20
The definition of the types used within the DHCPv4 option 43/DHCPv6 Option 17 depends on the vendor-class option reported 21
by the O-RU in its DHCP messages. 22
When a legacy O-RU reports its vendor-class using the “o-ran-ru” prefix, the following types are defined: 23
Type: 0x01 – O-RU Controller IP Address 24
Type: 0x02 – O-RU Controller Fully Qualified Domain Name 25
When the O-RU reports its vendor-class using the “o-ran-ru2” prefix, the following types are defined: 26
Type: 0x81 – O-RU Controller IP Address 27
Type: 0x82 – O-RU Controller Fully Qualified Domain Name 28
Type: 0x86 – O-RU Call home protocol 29
In all cases, the Type is followed by the length, which is the hexadecimal encoding of length of value field in octets , and the 30
Value. 31
When Type corresponds to an O -RU Controller IP Address , the value encodes IPv4 address(es) in hexadec imal format. For 32
example, a single server with IPv4 address 198.185.159.144 will be encoded in an option 43 TLV as 33
Type 0x81 (or x01 for legacy) 34
Length: 0x04  35
Value: C6 B9 9F 90 36
When Type corresponds to an O-RU Controller Fully Qualified Domain Name, this encodes the string representation of domain 37
name, using ACSII encoding (i.e., following for encoding used for the domain name in the Host Name DHCP Option 12). For 38
example, a server with FQDN “controller.operator.com” will be encoded in an option 43 TLV as 39
Type 0x82 (or x02 for legacy)  40
Length: 0x17  41
Value: 63 6F 6E 74 72 6F 6C 6C 65 72 2E 6F 70 65 72 61 74 6F 72 2E 63 6F 6D 42

The format of the DHCPv6 option 17 follows the format of the DHCPv4 encoding, with the additional inclusion of an Enterprise 1
Number prior to the TLV option data. The IANA allocated private enterprise number to be used with DHCPv6 option 17 is 2
53148. 3
When Type corresponds to the call home protocol, the value encodes whether an O-RU shall call home using NETCONF/SSH 4
or NETCONF/TLS using the IANA defined ports in [15]. If no call home protocol type is provided, the O -RU shall use 5

Value 01 -  O-RU shall attempt to call home using NETCONF/TLS 8

3.1.5 Multi-Vendor Plug-and-Play 14
As described in sub-section 3.3.2, an O-RU may optionally support certificate enrollment using CMPv2. 3GPP 32.509 15
specifies how the O-RU supporting IPv4 can discover the IP address or FQDN of one or more Certification Authority 16
(CA/RA) servers using DHCP Option 43. 17
An O-RU supporting IPv6 and certificate enrollment using CMPv2 shall additionally support the signaling of vendor specific 18
options using DHCPv6 option 17. The format of the DHCPv6 option 17 follows the format of the DHCPv4 encoding, with 19
the additional inclusion of an Enterprise Number prior to the TLV option data. The IANA allocated private enterprise number 20
to be used with DHCPv6 option 17 is 53148 (as allocated by IANA to O-RAN Alliance). 21
Note, in case of a point-to-point connection between the O-RU and the O-DU, the O-DU needs to provide means for 22
the O-RU to access the operator CA/RA for the O-RU certificate enrollment at the IP address conveyed as described 23
above. If the FQDN option is used instead, the O-DU needs to provide means for the O-RU to access an operator DNS 24
server in addition. 25
An O-RU shall report any discovered multi-vendor plug-and-play servers using the o-ran-dhcp YANG model. 26
3.1.6 Event-Collector Discovery  27
This section describes how an O -RU automatically discovers the Event-Collector to which it shall send its pnfRegistration 28
notification. The support by an O -RU of PNF Registration to a discovered Event-Collector is optional and hence this section 29
only applies to those O-RUs that support this optional capability.  30
O-RUs that have obtained their IPv6 addresses by stateless address auto -configuration, shall use stateless DHCPv6, RFC3736 31
[13], to obtain Event-Collector information. Other O-RUs operating using stateful IPv4 or IPv6 address allocations shall obtain 32
Event-Collector information during IP address allocation. Other O -RUs which have had their IP address(es) manually 33
configured, shall also have their Event-Collector(s) and Event-Collector Notification Format manually configured. 34
The O-RU shall be able to recover Event-Collector information using O-RAN defined vendor specific option to signal Event-35
Collector information to the O-RU using option 43 for DHCPv4 and option 17 for DHCPv6.  36
The definition of the types used within the DHCPv4 option 43/DHCPv6 Option 17 are as follows: 37
Type: 0x83 – Event-Collector IP Address 38
Type: 0x84 – Event-Collector Fully Qualified Domain Name 39
Type: 0x85 – Event-Collector Notification Format 40
In this version of the specification, the operation of an O -RU when receiving multiple instances of the Event-Collector IP 41
Address and/or Event-Collector FQDN information is not defined. 42

3.2 NETCONF Call Home to O-RU Controller(s) 28
The O-RU aims to have NETCONF sessions with all of the known O-RU Controller(s), either discovered using the DHCP 29
options defined in Section 3.1.4 , provisioned by an exis ting NETCONF client , or statically configured.  An O-RU controller 30
may attempt to autonomously initiate a NETCONF session with the O-RU, e.g., triggered by the pnfRegistration procedure. In 31
order to support NETCONF clients corresponding to known O-RU Controllers that either do not attempt to initiate a NETCONF 32
session with the O-RU, or are prohibited from doing so, e.g., because of Network Address Translation limitations, the O-RU 33
shall call home to all known O-RU Controllers with which it does not already have an active NETCONF session. 34
If the O-RU is unable to establish a NETCONF session with any of the O-RU Controller(s), the O-RU shall use the “re-call-35
home-no-ssh-timer” to repeatedly re -perform the call home procedure to all with which is does not have an established 36
NETCONF session.  37
Note, the same value of timer shall be used, irrespective of whether SSH or TLS is being used to transport the NETCONF 38
session. 39
The O-RU shall use RFC 8071 [15] whereby the O-RU (NETCONF Server) initiates a TCP connection to the NETCONF client. 40
The port used by the O-RU shall be the one signaled using the RFC 8572 DHCP option [14], else, if no port was signaled, the 41
O-RU shall use the IANA-assigned port 4334 to indicate that the O-RU wants to use SSHv2 to secure the NETCONF connection 42
and the IANA-assigned port 4335 to indicate that the O-RU wants to use TLS to secure the NETCONF connection . When the 43

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          30
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
NETCONF client accepts a TCP connection on the allocated port, it initiates an SSH session /TLS connection  with the 1
NETCONF Server. Using this SSH session/TLS connection, the NETCONF client initiates a NETCONF session. 2

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          31
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
The O-RU shall ensure that a persistent connection to any NETCONF client with “sudo” privileges is maintained by actively 1
testing the aliveness of the connection using the keep-alive mechanism defined in [15]. The establishment of NETCONF client 2
privileges is covered in Section 3.4. 3
3.3 NETCONF Connection Establishment 4
The identity of the NETCONF server (O-RU) shall be verified and authenticated by the NETCONF client according to local 5
policy before password-based authentication data or any configuration or state data is sent to or received from the NETCONF 6
server.  7
When using SSHv2, public key-based host authentication shall be used for authenticating the server (RFC 4253) by the clients. 8
In addition, server authentication based on X.509 certificates may also be provided [31]. 9
When using TLS, X.509 certificate-based authentication shall be used for mutual authentication between the NECTONF client 10
and NETCONF server.  11
Note: SSHv2 based public key-based host authentication requires that the SSH server ( O-RU) public keys are provisioned in 12
the NETCONF client (e.g., O-DU and/or SMO). As an alternative, RFC4251 mentions that “a possible strategy is to only accept 13
a host key without checking the first time a host is connected, save the key in a local database, and compare against that key on 14
all future connections to that host.”. This option simplifies the key management procedure as it doesn’t require to pre-populate 15
them in O-DU/SMO (SSH client) but obviously at the price of degraded security, therefore the support of this option shall be 16
configurable and left to operator’s choice. 17
3.3.1 NETCONF Security 18
As specified in clause 2.4, this version of the O -RU Management Plane Specification uses TLS 1.2 or SSHv2 for mutual 19
authentication between the NETCONF server (O -RU) and the NETCONF client (O -DU or SMO). Support for TLS 1.2 is 20
optional and support for SSHv2 is mandatory as described in Table 2. 21
If multiple NETCONF sessions are established to an O-RU, those sessions shall be established over separate SSH tunnels/TLS 22
connections. 23
3.3.2 NETCONF Authentication 24
This version of the O-RU Management Plane Specification supports SSHv2 using password authentication method for SSHv2 25
[6] and client authentication based on X.509 certificates [31] , as well as optional support for TLS 1.2 using X.509 certificate -26
based authentication. 27
The identity of the NETCONF server (O-RU) shall be verified and authenticated by the NETCONF client  (O-DU or SMO ) 28
according to local policy before authentication data or any configuration or state data is sent to or received from the server. 29
The identity of the NETCONF client (O -DU or SMO)  shall be verified and authenticated b y the NETCONF server (O-RU) 30
according to local policy (X.509 certificate-based or username/password) to ensure that the incoming NETCONF client request 31
is legitimate before any configuration or state data is se nt to or received from the NETCONF client. The server shall also 32
perform proper authorization of the client before accepting any request. 33
If authentication is based on X.509 certificates, for the purposes of user authentication, the mapping between certifi cates and 34
user names is provided by the SubjectAltName field of the X.509 certificate, which means that the user name is coded in the 35
subjectAltName. The username is determined from the subjectAltName using the rules defined in RFC 7589. For the purposes 36
of NETCONF server authentication, RFC 7589 [41] specifies server identity based on RFC 6125 [40]. 37
Upon initial system initialization, the O-RU is configured with a default account. The specific details of the default account are 38
to be agreed between operato r and vendor. An example of a default user account for account-type PASSWORD is one with 39
username “oranuser”. An example of a default user account for account -type CERTIFICATE is map type “san-rfc822-name” 40
with an rfc822-name of “oranuser@o-ran.org”. 41
The default account may be of account -type PASSWORD, in which case a default password also needs to be defined and 42
configured in the O-RU, for example “o-ran-password”. 43
 44

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          33
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Note: As the default account may be operator specific, this may require that the O-RU provides facilities to configure 1
securely this default account at installation time (i.e. before the O-RU is connected to the O-RU Controller). 2
If user authentication is based on X.509v3 certificate during O-RU plug and play, to support zero touch for the first NETCONF 3
connection, the O-RU shall support the default mapping between certificate and default NETCONF account which will map 4
any authenticated X.509 v3 certificate to this default O-RAN account. 5
Note: The trust anchor for O-RU shall be provisioned automatically with online CA server during O-RU Plug and 6
Play, and it must be same as the trust anchor of the O-RU Controller(s), thus avoiding the need for manual 7
configuration of the peer trust anchor for O-RU.  8
The default account is a member of the “sudo” access control group (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges) as it can 9
be used to create other accounts (see Section 3.3.3). 10
The identity of the SSH client (NETCONF client) shall be verified and authenticated by the SSH server (O-RU) according to 11
local policy to ensure that the incoming SSH client request is legitimate before any configuration or state data is sent to o r 12
received from the SSH client.  13
Upon initial system initialization, the NETCONF client can authenticate itself to the O-RU using SSH Authentication, with the 14
agreed default username and password. 15
If authentication based on X.509 certificates according to [31] is supported by SSH client and server, the certificates need to be 16
installed at initial system init ialization, or can be obtained through certificate enrolment with operator’s PKI (certificate 17
enrolment as defined by 3GPP with CMPv2 protocol between the NE and the operator’s CA). 18
3.3.3 User Account Provisioning 19
The NETCONF client with suitable privileges may provision user accounts on the O-RU, including the accounts (users) name, 20
password, group (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges) and whether a particular account is enabled or disabled.  21
• The username name is a str ing between 3 -32 characters. The first character must be a lowercase letter. The remaining 22
characters can be a lowercase letter or a number.  23
• The account-type is an enumeration, indicating whether password or certificate -based authentication is used for this 24
account. 25
• The password is a string between 8 -128 characters. Allowed characters in the password field include lowercase and 26
uppercase letters, numbers and the special characters: ! $ % ^ ( ) _ + ~ { } [ ] . – The password leaf is not present for those 27
user accounts associated with certificate-based authentication. 28
• The access control group associated with an account (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges). 29
• Whether an account is enabled. The YANG model ensures that at least one user account is always enabled on the O-RU 30
The new account information (user name, password, access group and whether the account is enabled) shall be stored in reset-31
persistent memory in O-RU. 32
If certificate based client authentication is used no password needs to be provisioned. At time of SSH connection, user’s 33
authorization is done based on the X.509 certificate’s SubjectAltName field that codes the associated account’s name. 34
When other user account (sudo) is created, the NETCONF client closes existing NETCONF session as described in section 3.7. 35
Then, the O-RU disables the default account and default account stays disabled over the resets. The default account becomes 36
enabled when the O-RU is reset to the factory default software by following the procedures defined in subsection 5.7. Any other 37
way to enable the default account is not precluded as O-RU vendor implementation matter. 38
The security principle defined in this section shall follow those defined for the default account and default mapping, i.e., the 39
O-RU Controller shall create a new mapping. 40
Note : Depending on the EE/CA certificate of the O-RU Controller, the map type can still be specified but with 41
specific fingerprint of the EE/CA certificate or based on SubjectAltName of EE/CA certificate as specified in sub-42
section 3.3.2 43

3.4 NETCONF Access Control 1
This subsection defines the access control for NETCONF clients. Its motivation is that when multiple NETCONF clients (users) 2
are defined, the NETCONF access control mechanism enables the NETCONF server to limit some operations for one client but 3
allow full access for another client. In particular, for hybrid access configuration as introduced in Chapter 2, this allows the 4
privileges associated with the NETCONF client in the O-DU to be distinct and different from the privileges associated with the 5
NETCONF client in the SMO. 6
In order to support interoperable access control management, the NETCONF Server shall use the IETF NETCONF Access 7
Control Model [RFC8341]. 8
Currently six access control groups are defined per NETCONF session: “sudo”, “smo”, “hybrid-odu”, “nms”, “fm-pm”, and 9
“swm”. The table below maps the group name to different privileges. Privileges are defined per namespace for read “R”, write 10
“W” and execute “X” rpc operations or subscribe to Notifications.  11
Note: when operating in hybrid management, the definition of above groupings does not preclude the NETCONF client in a 12
centralized network management system from being configured “sudo” privileges  that permit it to edit the configuration used 13
by an O-RU. However, importantly the operation of the O -DU in those situations may not be defined. For example, an O -DU 14
when operating with an O-RU which receives an autonomous reset RPC from a centralized NMS may not result in the O -DU 15
recovering the o-ran-operations:operational-info/operational-state/restart-cause from the O-RU to then determine that an 16
NMS triggered reset has been performed.  In order to r educe the possibility of such a scenario, it is recommended that when 17
operating in hybrid mode of operation, the NETCONF client in the O -DU is associated with the “hybrid-odu” privilege group 18
and the NETCONF client in the SMO is associated with the “smo” privilege group. 19

3.5 NETCONF capability discovery 5
The O-RU advertises its NETCONF capabilities in the NETCONF Hello message. The Hello message provides an indication 6
of support for standard features defined in NETCONF RFCs as well as support for specific namespaces. 7
NETCONF capabilities are exchanged between the O-RU and the NETCONF client(s). Examples of capabilities include [3]: 8
• Writable-running Capability 9
• Candidate Configuration Capability and associated Commit operation 10
• Discard change operation 11
• Lock and un-lock operations 12
• Confirmed commit Capability 13
• Cancel commit operation 14
• Rollback on error capability 15
• Validate Capability 16
• Startup configuration capability 17
• URL capability 18
• XPATH capability 19
• Notifications 20
• Interleave capability 21
All O-RAN O-RUs shall support the XPATH capability, NETCONF Notifications and at least one of the writeable-running and 22
candidate configuration capabilities. 23
The NETCONF client uses the get RPC together with sub-tree based <filter> and XPATH based <filter> to recover particular 24
sub-trees from the O-RU. Please see Chapter 6 for more information on NETCONF based configuration management. 25
In order to avoid interactions between the operation of supervision watchdog timer (see section 3.6) and the confirmed commit 26
timer (default value set to 600 seconds in RFC 6241), when using the NETCONF confirmed commit capability, a NECTONF 27
client with “sudo” privileges shall ensure the confirmed -timeout is less than the supervision-notification-interval timer 28
(default value 60 seconds in o-ran-supervision.yang).  29

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          37
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
3.6 Monitoring NETCONF connectivity 1
When having a session with a NETCONF client with “sudo” or “hybrid-odu” access privileges, the O-RU operates a watchdog 2
supervision timer to ensure that the session to the NECTONF client is persistent, as described in section 3.4. Additionally, the 3
O-RU provides NETCONF Notifications to indicate to remote systems that its management system is operational. This 4
supervision is intended to be used with the NETCONF client associated with the operation of the peer to the O-RAN Radio’s 5
lower layer split. 6
Note, if another NETCONF client is discovered or configured, e.g., in hybrid mode of operation, and is used to establish 7
a NETCONF session with “sudo” access privil eges, the same watchdog supervision rules shall apply, meaning that a 8
NETCONF server shall support the operation of individual supervision watchdog timers for each NETCONF client with 9
“sudo” or “hybrid-odu” privileges . 10
The NETCONF client is responsible fo r automatically enabling the operation of the supervision watchdog timer  by creating 11
supervision-notification subscription, whenever the O-RU has an established NETCONF session to a client with “sudo” or 12
“hybrid-odu” privileges.  13
The O-RU uses two timers, referred generically as watchdog timers, to support the bi -directional monitoring of NETCONF 14
connectivity; 15
• Notification timer: 16
Value: Equal to supervision-notification-interval (default value: 60s) 17
Operation: The O-RU sends supervision-notification to those NETCONF clients that have subscribed to receive such 18
notifications. The O-RU sends supervision-notification, at the latest when the timer expires. The O -RU Controller 19
confirms that NETCONF connectivity to the O-RU is operational by receiving the notification.  20
• Supervision timer: 21
Value : Equal to supervision-notification-interval (default value: 60s) + guard-timer-overhead (default : 10s) 22
Operation: The O-RU goes into supervision failure operation when the timer expires. This means that a NETCONF 23
client with sudo privileges should repeatedly reset this supervision timer. The O-RU confirms that NETCONF 24
connectivity to the O-RU Controller is operational.  25
 26
The O-RU enables watchdog timers when it receives an rpc create-subscription from a NETCONF client with sudo privileges. 27
The notification timer shall start when the O -RU receives a create -subscription rpc, but how the O -RU treats the supervi sion 28
timer is up to O-RU’s implementation based on the above definition. After the watchdog timers have been enabled, the O-RU 29
is responsible for sending supervision-notification after the expiry of the notification timer. An O-RU Controller with “sudo” 30
or “hybrid-odu” privileges shall be prepared to receive supervision-notification at any time when the watchdog timers are 31
enabled. 32
The NETCONF client is responsible for sending supervision-watchdog-reset RPC in order not to cause the Supervision timer 33
to expire, and the O-RU should send next notification timestamp  as next-update-at in reply. (Note : next-update-at is just 34
informative). In the supervision-watchdog-reset RPC, the NETCONF client may configure new value s for the watchdog 35
timers. When the O-RU receives an rpc supervision-watchdog-reset, it is responsible for resetting its supervision timer and 36
notification timer. 37
The NETCONF client can set new value of watchdog timer without receiving supervision-notification from the O-RU. The 38
new value is taken into use immediately with respect to supervision-watchdog-reset RPC content. The next notification should 39
be expected not later than at the moment addressed in timestamp provided by RPC reply. 40
Note, if another NETC ONF client has locked the running configuration, e.g., when operating in hybrid mode of 41
operation, and if the O -RU Controller attempts to configure a new value of the watchdog timer(s) by sending the 42
supervision-watchdog-reset RPC, then the RPC operation t o reset the watchdog timer will succeed, but the related 43
backend implementation to modify the watchdog timer(s) may fail. In such circumstances, the O-RU may use the error-44
message in the RPC output to indicate to the O-RU Controller that the configuration modification has failed. 45
If the supervision timer expires, the O-RU will enter “supervision failure” condition, as described in Chapter 11 . If all 46
NETCONF sessions to NECTONF clients with “sudo” privileges are closed, the O-RU shall immediately disable operation of 47
the supervision timer. 48

3.7 Closing a NETCONF Session 4
A NETCONF client closes an existing NETCONF session by issuing the RPC close-session command. The O-RU shall respond 5
and close the SSH session or TLS connection. The O-RU shall then re-commence call home procedures, as described in Section 6
3.2. 7
Note, under normal operations, it is expected that at least one NETCONF session with “sudo” or “hybrid-odu” privileges are 8
long-lived and used to repeatedly reset the O-RU’s supervision watchdog timer.  NECTONF clients associated with other  9
privilege groups are not expected to operate using persistent NETCONF sessions. 10
Note, if a NETCONF client has been previously become known to an O -RU by being configured using NETCONF, and the 11
NETCONF client is subsequently removed from the O -RU’s configuration, e.g., by a second NETCONF client with “sudo” 12
privileges, the NETCONF server shall force the termination of the NETCONF session to the removed client.  13
3.8 PNF Registration  14
The support by an O-RU of PNF Registration to a discovered Event-Collector is optional and hence this section only applies to 15
those O-RUs that support this optional capability. An O-RU that support pnfRegistration shall also support the Monitoring the 16
Communications Channel between O-RU and Event-Collector as defined in sub-section 15.6. 17
3.8.1 PNF Registration Procedure 18
The pnfRegistration notification is a JSON encoded message sent from the O -RU to the discovered Event-Collector using 19
REST/HTTPS. As a pre -condition to performing PNF Registration, the O -RU first receives the Event -Collector information 20
encoded in a DHCP/DHCPv6 option as described in sub-section 3.1.6. The O-RU shall attempt to establish a HTTP connection 21
to the discovered Event-Collector using TLS to authenticate the connection. It shall then signal the pnfRegistration notification 22
over the HTTP/TLS connection . The sending of the pnfRegistration notification is repeated periodically until the SMO 23
establishes a NETCONF session with the O-RU. 24
An O -RU that is performing the PNF registration procedure whilst simultaneously performing the call home procedure 25
described in sub-section 3.2, shall be able to determine that the SMO has established a NETCONF session with the O-RU. This 26
is identified by the O-RU analyzing the source IP address from which the NETCONF originates, based on the assumption that 27
the NETCONF session from the SMO originates from an IP address that is distinct from the IP address(es) of the “known O -28
RU Controller(s)” to which the O-RU is simultaneously performing the call home procedure.  29
 30

3.8.2 Encoding of PNF Registration Notification 3
In this version of the specification, the encoding of the pnfRegistration notification follows the ONAP definition [37]. 4
The pnfRegistration notification shall include the IP address information necessary for a NETCONF client to establish IP 5
connectivity to the NETCONF Server in the O-RU, i.e., shall include the field oamV4IpAddress when the O-RU has a 6
configured IPv4 interface and/or the field oamV6IpAddress when the O-RU has a configured IPv6 interface. 7
The contents of the pnfRegistration notification are derived from the O-RU’s configuration database. An O-RU shall support 8
the o-ran-hardware.yang model revision 5.0.0, or later, which defines the schema nodes corresponding to unitFamily and 9
unitType values and the o-ran-operations.yang model revision 5.0.0, or later, which defines the schema nodes corresponding 10
to the version of pnfRegistration fields. 11
