Chapter 4 O-RU to O-DU Interface Management  2
An O -RU has a number of network interfaces, including Ethernet , VLAN  and IP interfaces. This section describes the 3
management of these network interfaces.  4
4.1 O-RU Interfaces 5
The O-RU’s configuration for its interfaces is defined using the o-ran-interfaces.yang module. This module augments the 6
standard ietf -interfaces.yang and ietf -ip.yang modules. The O-RU’s interfaces are built on a layering principle  where each 7
interface has a unique name.  8
All interfaces are referenced by their port-number and name. The base interface corresponds to the Ethernet interface. These 9
leafs describe the maximum transmission unit (l2-mtu), the hardware-address as well as optional alias mac addressees that may 10
be used to transport the CU plane. Above the Ethernet interface are VLAN interfaces. Both Ethernet and VLAN interfaces can 11
support IP interfaces. IP interfaces are defined using the standard ietf -ip.yang model. Accordingly, each IP interface can have 12
an IPv4 and/or IPv6 interface(s) defined. Operational state associated with these interfaces provide additional detail of the layer 13
3 configuration, including prefix(es), domain name servers and default gateway addresses. 14
Finally, leafs associated with CoS and DSCP marking are defined, enabli ng independent configuration of CoS and DSCP 15
markings for u-plane, c -plane and m -plane traffic. As a default, all user -plane flows are marked identically by the O-RU. 16
Optionally, the interfaces can be configured to support enhanced user plane marking for u p-link traffic whereby different CoS 17
or DSCP values can be configured. This enables individual receive endpoints in the O-RU to be configured with different 18
markings to then enable differentiated handling of up-link flows by the transport system. 19
Because the o-ran-interfaces model defines augments to the ietf -interfaces model, the O-RU can leverage the definition of 20
operational state in ietf-interfaces to optionally report packet and byte counts on a per interface basis.  A single RPC is defined 21
in the o-ran-interfaces module, to enable these counters to be reset. 22

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          42
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
4.2 Transceiver 1
The o-ran-transceiver YANG module is used to define operational state for the pluggable transceiver module (like SFP, SFP+, 2
SFP28, XFP and QSFP, QSFP+, QSFP28, QSFP56 ). Each transceiver is associated with a unique interface-name and port-3
number. 4
A digital diagnostic monitoring interface for optical transceivers is used to allow access to device operating parameters. As  5
specified in SFF-8472 [16] and SFF-8636 [34], data is typically retrieved from the transceiver module in a file. This file may 6
be obtained from O-RU by the NETCONF client. Please see Chapter 9 for more details. 7
With QSFP form factor, the optical links may be multi -wavelengths (4xTx & 4xRx) and/or mu lti-fibers (MPO - Multifiber 8
Parallel Optic). The QSFP digital diagnostic interface [34] describes the use of optical lanes and the O -RU interface 9
management defines alarm 29 :“transceiver fault” for all media lanes. 10
The byte with offset i (i=0, …, 511) from the beginning of the file is the byte read from data address i of the transceiver memory 11
at two-wire interface address 0xA0 if i<256, otherwise it is the byte read from data address i-256 of the transceiver memory at 12
two-wire interface address 0xA2. The retrieved data is stored in the file without any conversion in binary format. 13
The O-RU stores data from the transceiver module on transceiver module detection during startup. The data from the transceiver 14
module is saved in the file. A NETCONF client can upload it by using the File Upload procedure defined in chapter 9. The O-15
RU does not synchronize contents of the file with transceiver memory in runtime, therefore bytes representing dynamic 16
information are expected to be outdated . The O-RU does not remove the file on transceiver module removal. If a transceiver 17
module is inserted during File Upload procedure then the procedure may provide a file with previous content or fail (with failure 18
reason as listed in File Upload procedure). If the O-RU is unable to retrieve the data from the transceiver module or it is not 19
present then the O-RU does not create the file or removes the file created earlier (note that File Upload procedure requesting 20
non-existing file shall fail).  21
The file name shall have the following syntax: 22
sfp_{portNumber}.sffcap 23
where {portNumber} is the value of port-number leaf of the corresponding list of port -transceiver data. Examples: 24
sfp_0.sffcap, sfp_1.sffcap. 25
4.3 C/U Plane VLAN Configuration 26
Within the o-ran-interfaces YANG model, each named Ethernet interface includes a leaf to indicate whether VLAN tagging is 27
supported. By default, VLAN tagging is enabled on all interfaces. This permits an O-RU to autonomously discover that it is 28
connected to a trunk port, as described in Section 3.1.2. 29
When an O-RU is connected to a trunk port, VLANs will also typically be assigned to the C/U plane connections. The VLAN(s) 30
used to support C/U plane transport may be different from the VLAN(s) used to support management plane  connectivity. The 31
VLAN assigned to the U-Plane must be the same as the VLAN assigned to the C-Plane for any given eAxC_ID. When different 32
VLANs are used, the C/U plane VLANs shall be configured in the O-RU by the NETCONF client. In such circumstances, as 33
defined in o-ran-interfaces, the NETCONF client shall configure separate named interfaces for each active VLAN. This 34
configuration will define a C/U-Plane named VLAN interface as being the higher-layer-if reference for the underlying Ethernet 35
interface and the underlying Ethernet interface is defined as being the lower-layer-if reference for the named VLAN interface. 36
4.4 O-RU C/U Plane IP Address Assignment 37
In this release, the support for C/U plane transport over UDP/IP is optional and hence this section only applies to those O-RUs 38
that support this optional capability. 39
An O-RU that supports C/U plane transport over UDP/IP shall support IPv4 and /or IPv6 based transport. A NETCONF client 40
can receive a hint as to whether an O-RU supports a particular IP version by using the get rpc to recover the list of interfaces 41
supported by the O-RU and using the presence of the augmented ipv4 container or ipv6 container in the o-ran-interfaces YANG 42
module as an indication that a particular IP version is supported. 43
The IP interface(s) used to support UDP/IP based C/U plane transport may be different than the IP interface(s) used to support 44
management plane connectivity. When different IP interface(s) is/are used, the C/U plane IP interfaces shall be confi gured in 45

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          43
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
the O-RU by the NETCONF client by using the ietf-ip YANG model to configure the IPv4 container and/or IPv6 container. 1
When defined by the NETCONF client, this interface shall be configured using either a named Ethernet interface (i.e., where 2
the interface type is set to ianaift:ethernetCsmacd) and/or a named VLAN interface  (i.e., where the interface type is set to 3
ianaift:l2vlan), depending upon whether VLANs are used to support IP based C/U plane traffic. 4
When a separate C/U plane IP interface is configured by the NETCONF client, additionally the NETCONF client may statically 5
configure the IP address(es) on this/these interface(s). If the NETCONF client does not statically configure an IP address, the 6
O-RU shall be responsible for performing IP address assignment procedures on the configured interfaces. 7
When an O-RU has not been configured with a static IP address , the O-RU shall support the IP address assignment using the 8
following techniques: 9
When the O-RU supports IPv4: 10
1. IPv4 configuration using DHCPv4 [10]. 11
and when the O-RU supports IPv6: 12
2. IPv6 Stateless Address Auto-Configuration (SLAAC) [11]. 13
3. IPv6 State-full address configuration uses DHCPv6 [12]. 14
4.5 Definition of processing elements 15
The CU-plane application needs to be uniquely associated with specific data flows. This association is achieved by defining an 16
O-RU “processing element” which can then be associated with a particular C /U plane endpoint address [2] or de lay 17
measurement operation. Unless specified otherwise, a common processing element is required to be configured for the control 18
and user-plane application components associated with any individual eAxC_ID. 19
The O-RU management plane supports different optio ns for defining the transport -based endpoint identifiers used by a 20
particular processing element (used depending on transport environment), supporting the following 3 options: 21
• Processing element definition based on usage of different (alias) MAC addresses; 22
• Processing element definition based on a combination of VLAN identity and MAC address; and 23
• Processing element definition based on UDP-ports and IP addresses. 24
Note: there is no well-defined source port currently allocated by IANA for the o-ran application and hence the NETCONF 25
client is responsible for configuring this port number in the O-RU.  26
A processing element defines both the local and remote endpoints used with a specific data flow. The processing element 27
definition includes its element name which is then used by other systems to refer to a particular processing element instance. 28
The o-ran-interfaces YANG model is used to define feature support for C/U plane transport based on alias MAC addresses and 29
UDP/IP. The exchange of NETCONF capabilities is used to signal which optional capabilities are supported by the O-RU, as 30
described in Annex C. 31
The o-ran-processing-elements YANG model uses a processing-elements container to define a list of processing elements. 32
Each processing element is identified b y a unique element  name. Each processing element references a particular interface-33
name used to support the data flows associated with a particular processing element. Depending upon the type of C/U plane 34
transport session, additionally leafs are configured that specify MAC addresses, and/or VLANs and/or IP addresses and/or UDP 35
ports used to identify a particular processing element. 36
The O-RU may discard any received CU-plane messages , i.e., eCPRI/IEEE 1914 frames/packets, which are not transported 37
using a configured processing element. 38
4.6 O-DU Verification of C/U Plane Transport Connectivity  39
As described above, there will likely be multiple C/ U-plane data flows being exchanged between the O-DU and the O-RU. In 40
order to enable checks verifying end -to-end transport connectivity between the O-DU and O-RU, the O-RU shall support 41
transport connectivity check capabilities using a request/reply function.  42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          44
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Using that connectivity monitoring procedure, reachability/connectivity checks between user plane endpoints can be performed 1
by the O-DU: 2
- During O-RU configuration, to validate the transport configuration 3
- At runtime to monitor network connectivity 4
In packet networks connectivity checking is usually done by exchanging probe-messages between the endpoints. The periodicity 5
of this exchange depends on the use case. For availability measurement, the only use case relevant for this specification, the 6
periodicity is usually between 1 and 60 seconds. 7
Two different network protocols are defined for performing the transport connectivity check procedure: 8
- For C/U sessions over Ethernet: Loop -back Protocol (LB/LBM) as defined by IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag) 9
[17]. 10
- When the O-RU supports C/U sessions over IP: UDP echo, RFC 862 [18]. 11
 12
Figure 9: C/U Plane Transport Connectivity Verification 13
4.6.1 Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure 14
If the O-RU and O-DU are operating their C/U sessions on Ethernet, the transport connectivity verification checks operate at 15
the Ethernet layer. In this O-RU Management Plane Specification, the protocol for Ethernet connectivity monitoring is based 16
on the Loop-back Protocol as defined by IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag) [17].  17
For the purpose of connectivity monitoring all C/U -plane messaging endpoints in the fronthaul network are part of the same 18
Maintenance Entity (ME). They each get the assigned the role of a Maintenance association End Point (MEP) for LBM. 19
The sending of Loop-back Messages (LBMs) is administratively initiated and stopped in the O-DU. Therefore, sending LBM 20
requests needs to be requested by an administration entity, specifying an Ethernet MAC address assigned to the O-RU responder. 21
In this O-RU Management Plane Specification requests are always sent from an O-DU to a unicast Ethernet MAC address of 22
an O-RU. 23

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          45
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
4.6.1.1 Validating the transport configuration 1
After setting up a U/C-plane session between an O-DU and an O-RU, the O-DU can test whether connectivity exists as per the 2
configuration. To achieve that, at the time a U/C-plane messaging endpoint becomes operational at an O-RU, it starts an LBM 3
responder application which automatically responds to incoming LBM requests on that endpoint. Based on a configuration 4
command the O-DU starts sending out a predefined number of LBM requests to its O-RU(s) at a predefined interval, storing 5
the information received in LBM responses from the O-RU(s) in an internal database. O-RU(s) are identified by both Ethernet 6
MAC address and the CU plane VLAN.  7
Note, the O-RU shall be able to respond to LoopBack Messages received from different remote Maintenance Association 8
Endpoints 9
In case the configuration of the session is indeed correct, the O-DU should receive LBM responses from the O-RU(s) within a 10
time frame dependent on the network latency and the O-RU’s reaction time. If LBMs from the O-RU(s) are being received, the 11
session is determined to be operational. 12
4.6.1.2 Monitor network connectivity 13
After the procedure described in section 4.6.1.1 has been executed successfully, a further procedure may be executed 14
continuously to maintain the connectivity status. To achieve this the O-DU continues to send out LBM requests at the configured 15
interval. It also keeps track of LBM responses received.  16
Based on the LBM responses received the O-DU shall decide on the connectivity status. Connectivity shall be assumed to be 17
available as long as LBM responses from the O-RU(s) are being received at the configured interval. Connectivity shall be 18
assumed not available if no LBM response from the particular O-RU has been received for an interval that is as long as 3 x the 19
configured LBM request interval or longer. 20
4.6.1.3 Managing Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure 21
An O-DU may have one or more Ethernet interfaces that have to support the Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure. This 22
section describes the management of this function. The module described here is based on (i.e. a subset of) the mef-cfm module 23
defined by the Metro Ethernet Forum [19]. This is to allow for a later extension of the module to the full feature set of mef-cfm.  24
The YANG module provided below supports the configuration and fault management of the Loop-back Protocol as defined by 25
IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag). 26
Derived from MEF CFM YANG, the subset of type definitions are defined as part of the o-ran-lbm.yang. 27
4.6.2 IP connectivity monitoring procedure 28
If the O-RU and O-DU are connected usi ng IP (and UDP/IP is being used to transport the C/U plane), these transport 29
connectivity verification checks operate at layer 3. Layer 3 connection verification is based on the O-RU supporting the UDP 30
echo server functionality, RFC 862 [18]. The NETCONF client is responsible for enabling the UDP echo server in the O-RU, 31
triggering the O-RU to listen for UDP datagrams on the well-known port 7. When a datagram is received by the O-RU, the data 32
from it is sent back towards the sender, where its receipt can be used to confirm UDP/IP connectivity between the endpoints. 33
4.6.2.1 Managing IP Connectivity Monitoring Procedure 34
This section describes the management of the UDP echo functionality. The NETCONF client uses the enable-udp-echo leaf in 35
the udp-echo YANG model to control operation of the UDP echo server in the O-RU. The NETCONF client is able to control 36
the DSCP marking used by the O-RU when it echoes back datagrams using the dscp-config leaf. Additionally, the NETCONF 37
client can recover the number of UDP Echo messages sent by the O-RU by using echo-replies-transmitted operational state. 38
An O-DU may have one or more IP interfaces that have to support the UDP/IP connectivity monitoring procedure. An O-RU 39
with its UDP echo server enabled shall be able to respond to UDP datagrams originated from any valid source IP address. 40
4.7 C/U-Plane Delay Management  41
The Intra-PHY lower layer fronthaul split has the characteristic of a stringent bandwidth and tight latency requirement. The 42
CUS-Plane specification [2] describes how the propagation delay incurred due to distance between the O-DU and O-RU is an 43
important parameter in defining the optimization of windowing and receive -side buffering operations. This section describes 44
the procedures that are used to manage the delay parameters for the fronthaul split.  45

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          46
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
4.7.1 Delay Parameters 1
The reference points for delay management are introduced in [2] and included for reference in Figure 10. 2
 3
Figure 10: Definition of reference points for delay management 4
Important delay paramet ers related to the operation of the O-RU are referred to as the O-RU delay profile. As the delay 5
characteristics for an O-RU may vary based on air interface properties, a table of the parameters is provided based on a 6
combination of sub -carrier spacing (SCS) and channel bandwidth . When considering the downlink data direction, these 7
parameters include: 8
T2a_min :  Corresponding t o the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving the last data sample over the 9
fronthaul interface and transmitting the first IQ sample at the antenna. 10
T2a_max: Corresponding to the earliest allowable time when a data packet is received before th e corresponding firs IQ 11
sample is transmitted at the antenna. 12
Using the above parameters, (T2a_max – T2a_min): The difference between these two parameters corresponds to the O-RU 13
reception window range. 14
T2a_min_cp_dl: Corresponding to the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving downlink real time control 15
plane message over the fronthaul interface and transmitting the corresponding first IQ sample at the antenna. 16
T2a_max_cp_dl: Corresponding to the earliest allowable time when a downlink real time control message is received before 17
the corresponding first IQ sample is transmitted at the antenna. 18
Tcp_adv_dl: Corresponding to the time difference (advance) between the reception window for downlink real time Control 19
messages and reception window for the corresponding IQ data messages. 20
The delay parameters related to the operation of the O-RU for the uplink data direction include: 21
Ta3_min: Corresponding to the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving an IQ sample at the antenna and 22
transmitting the first data sample over the fronthaul interface. 23
Ta3_max: Corresponding to the maximum O-RU data processing delay between receiving an IQ sample at the antenna and 24
transmitting the last data sample over the fronthaul interface. 25
Using the above parameters, (Ta3_max – Ta3_min): The difference between these two parameters corresponds to the O-RU 26
transmission window range. 27
T2a_min_cp_ul: The minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving real time up-link control plane message over 28
the fronthaul interface and receiving the first IQ sample at the antenna. 29
T2a_max_cp_ul: The earliest allowable time when a real time up-link control message is received before the corresponding 30
first IQ sample is received at the antenna. 31
When requested, all O-RUs shall signal the table of statically “pre -defined” values of the above parameters, for different 32
supported combinations of SCS and channel bandwidth over the management plane interface. This will typically occur during 33
the initial startup phase. 34
4.7.2 Reception Window Monitoring 35
The O-RU shall monitor operation of its reception window, monitoring the arrival of packets received over the fronthaul 36
interface relative to the earliest and latest allowable times as defined by the values of T2a_max and T2a_min respectively. 37
See Annex B.2 for information on reception window counters. 38

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
4.8 O-RU Adaptive Delay Capability 1
O-RUs may optionally support the ability to optimize their buffers based on information signalled concerning the configuration 2
of the O-DU, e.g., including the O-DU delay profile, together with transport delay information, which may have been derived 3
by the O-DU by using a delay measurement procedures operated by the O-DU or by other techniques.  This section describes 4
such optional O-RU buffer optimization functionality.  5
An O-RU that supports the optional adaptive timing capability shall indicate such to the O-RU Controller client by exchanging 6
NETCONF capabilities, as described in Section 6.2 and Annex C indicating that it supports the ADAPTIVE-O-RU-PROFILE 7
feature. An O-RU Controller may then provide the O-RU with the O-DU delay profile based on a combination of sub-carrier 8
spacing (SCS) and channel bandwidth, comprising the following parameters: 9
T1a_max_up: Corresponding to the earliest possible time which the O-DU can support transmitting an IQ data message 10
prior to transmission of the corresponding IQ samples at the antenna 11
TXmax: Corresponding to the maximum amount of time which the O-DU requires to transmit all downlink user plane IQ 12
data message for a symbol. 13
Ta4_max: Corresponding to the latest possible time which the O-DU can support receiving the last uplink user plane IQ 14
data message for a symbol 15
RXmax: Corresponding to the maximum time difference the O-DU can support between receiving the first user plane IQ 16
data message for a symbol and receiving the last user plane IQ data message for the same symbol. 17
T1a_max_cp_dl: Corresponding to the earliest possible time which the O -DU can support transmitting the downlink real 18
time control message prior to transmission of the corresponding IQ samples at the antenna. 19
In addition to the O-DU delay profile, the O-RU-Controller provides the O-RU with the transport network timing parameters: 20
T12_min: Corresponding to the minimum delay between any O-DU and O-RU processing elements 21
T12_max:  Corresponding to the maximum delay between O-DU and O-RU processing elements 22
T34_min: Corresponding to the minimum delay between any O-RU and O-DU processing elements 23
T34_max:  Corresponding to the maximum delay between O-RU and O-DU processing elements 24
The O-RU may use this information to adapt its delay profile, ensuring that the inequalities defined in Annex B of [2] are still 25
valid  26
The O-RU controller will typically provide this information during the O-RU’s start-up procedure. If an O-RU receives the 27
adaptive delay configuration information when operating a carrier, the O-RU shall not adapt its O-RU delay profile until all 28
carriers operating using the O-RU buffers have been disabled. Once an O-RU has adapted its O-RU profile, it will include the 29
newly adapted timing values when signaling its delay parameters to a NETCONF client. 30
4.9 Measuring transport delay parameters 31
An O-RU may optionally indicate that it supports the eCPRI based measurement of transport delays between O-DU and O-RU, 32
as described in [2].  33
When indicated that it supports the optional eCPRI based delay measurement, an O-RU shall support the processing of delay 34
measurement messages at any time, including whenever the C/U plane is configured. As well as the O-RU including its timing 35
compensation values in the eCPRI delay measurement messages (tcv1 and tcv2 shown in the figure below), the YANG model 36
additionally enables a NETCONF client to recover these parameters from the O-RU over the M-Plane interface. 37

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          48

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 11: eCPRI One-Way Delay Measurement procedure [2] 2
An O-RU that supports the eCPRI based delay measurement capability, shall be able to support simultaneous operation of delay 3
measurements over any processing element configured as described in section 4.5. For each processing element configured for 4
use by the del ay measurement procedure, the O-RU shall keep a record of the number of responses, requests and follow -up 5
messages transmitted by the O-RU. 6
4.10 O-RU Monitoring of C/U Plane Connectivity  7
The O-RU is responsible for monitoring the C/U plane connection and raising an alarm if the logical C/U -plane connection 8
associated with a processing -element fails. The O -RU uses a timer to monitor the C/U plane connection on a per processing -9
element basis. This timer is enabled only when at least one array-carrier using the processing-element is in the active state and 10
is reset whenever it receives any C/U plane data flows associated with the particular processing-element. Because of the variety 11
of PHY and C/U plane configurations, the O-RU cannot independently determine the minimum frequency of messages across 12
the fronthaul interface. Therefore, as a default, the O -RU shall use a timer value of 160 milliseconds for monitoring the C/U 13
plane connection. An O-RU may indicate that its C/U-plane monitoring timer is configurable, by the presence of the cu-plane-14
monitoring container in the o-ran-supervision.yang model. A NETCONF client can use the container to configure the O-RU’s 15
timer value, including being able to disable the operation of C/U Plane monitoring. 16
Note, if the O-RU supports this timer, then depending on how long the O-DU takes to initiate sending of C/U plane data 17
flows, it may be advisable for the NETCONF client to initially disable the operation of the timer before carrier activation. 18
Such an approach will avoid the O-RU sending spurious alarm notifications triggered by O-DU delays in initializing the 19
sending of C/U plane data that exceed the default timer value. Once C/U plane data flows have commenced, the NECTONF 20
client can re-configure the timer with the desired value and hence activate monitoring of the C/U plane connectivity by the O-21
RU. 22
 23

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          49
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
4.11 Bandwidth Management 1
An O-RU can indicate the maximum bitrate able to be supported on those interfaces associated with a particular physical port 2
using the optional nominal-bitrate leaf in the o -ran-transceiver YANG module. When the sustainable bitrate able to be 3
supported by an O -RU is less than the combined bitrates of all its physical ports, an O -RU can use the optional interface-4
grouping container in the o -ran-interfaces YANG model to define the maximum sustainable rate able to be supported by an 5
interface-group-id corresponding to a group of one or more physical interfaces. The same YANG model is used to augment 6
the ietf-interfaces defined interface list with the interface-group-id to which the interface belongs. 7
Note, the maximum sustainable bandwidth is calculated over one radio frame, meaning that the peak bandwidth can 8
exceed the defined value over time periods shorter than one radio frame. 9
Chapter 5 Software Management 10
The Software Management function provides a set of operations allowing the desired software build to be downloaded, installed 11
and activated at O-RU. Successful software activation operation does not mean an O-RU is running the just activated software 12
build. An O-RU reset RPC is required to trigger the O-RU to take the activated software build into operational use. 13
A single software build is considered as set of internally consistent files compliant within such a build. Replacement of files 14
within a build is prohibited, as this will cause software version incompatibility. Software build is a subject of versioning and 15
maintenance and as such cannot be broken. 16
The use of compression and ciphering for the content of the software build is left to vendor implementation. The only file which 17
shall never be ciphered is the manifest.xml file.  18
It is also Vendor's responsibility to handle SW Build / package / file integrity check. 19
The O-RU provides a set of so called "software slots" or "slots". Each slot provides an independent storage location for a single 20
software build. The number of slots offered by O-RU depends on the device’s capabilities. At least two writable slots shall be 21
available at the O-RU for failsafe update operation. Presence of read only slot is optional. The software slots are resources 22
provided by the O-RU and as such are not the subject of creation and deletion. The size of individual software slots is fixed and 23
determined by the O-RU's vendor and sufficient to accommodate the full software build. 24
Note: procedures used in Software Management are covered by o-ran.software-management.yang module. 25
5.1 Software Package 26
The software package is delivered by the O-RU vendor. 27
Each software package includes: 28
- manifest.xml 29
- software files to be installed on O-RU 30
 31
The name of package should follow the following format: 32
“<Vendor Code><Vendor Specific Field>[#NUMBER].EXT” 33
Where: 34
- Vendor Code is a mandatory part which has two capital characters, 35
- Vendor Specific Field is any set of characters allowed in filename. The value must not include character “_” (underscore) 36
or “#” (hash). The value can be defined per vendor for the human readable information. Version information is necessary 37
in the Vendor Specific Field which defines load version, 38
- NUMBER is optional and used when the original file is split into smaller pieces – number after “#” indicates the number 39
of a piece. Numbering starts from 1 and must be continuous, 40

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          50
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
- EXT is a mandatory part which defines the extension of filename. A vendor provides one or more software packages. Each 1
software package shall be compressed by zip. 2
Note: the name of package needs a <Vendor Code> prefix to avoid issue if two vendors provide files with same name. 3
Note: the NETCONF client shall support ZIP functionality to enable support of compressed files types.  4
Note: the operator needs to manage and control which O-RU files will be stored and used in the file server, e.g., based on O-5
RU files provided by O-RU vendors and network configurations. The operator needs to make sure that only the expected version 6
of O-RU files will be transferred from the file server to the O-RU. Different versions of files for O-RU with the same vendor 7
and same product code should be avoided. 8
The content of the manifest.xml file allows to maintain software update process correctly in terms of compatibility between O-9
RU hardware and software build to be downloaded. The content of the Manifest file prohibits the O-RU from installing software 10
builds designed for device based on different hardware. The format of the manifest.xml file is: 11
<xml> 12
<manifest version=”1.0”> /// @version describes version of file format (not the content) 13
 <products> 14
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x11” name=”RUXX.x11” build-Id=”1”/>  15
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x12” name=”RUXX.x12” build-Id=”1”/> 16
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818818\…” name=”RUYY” build-Id=”2”/>  17
  /// @vendor is as reported by O-RU 18
  /// @code is a regular expression that is checked against productCode reported by O-RU 19
  /// @name is optional and used for human reading – MUST NOT be used for other purposes! 20
  /// @buildId is value of build@id (see below) 21
 </products> 22
 <builds> 23
  <build id=”1” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 24
  /// @id is index of available builds. 25
  /// @bldName and @bldVersion are used in YANG (build-name, build-version) 26
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 27
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 28
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 29
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 30
   /// @fileName and @fileVersion are used in YANG (name, version) 31
   /// @path is full path (with name and extension) of a physical file, relative to package 32
root folder,used in YANG (local-path) 33
   /// @checksum is used to chech file integrity on O-RU side 34
  </build> 35
  <build id=”2” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 36
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 37
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 38
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 39
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 40
   <file fileName=”zzzz” fileVersion=”1.5” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 41
package -root-folder” checksum=”ABCDEF”/ > 42
  </build> 43
 </builds> 44
</manifest> 45
</xml> 46
 47

- XML tag "code" corresponds to content of leaf "product-code", 51

- XML tag "bldVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "build-version", 54

5.2 Software Inventory 1
Pre-condition:  2
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 3
Post-condition: 4
- NETCONF client successfully collected the software inventory information from NETCONF server. 5
 6
Figure 12: Inventory fetch call flow 7
Software Inventory is fetched by a NETCONF Client using the NETCONF get rpc filtered over the software-slot container. 8
The response contains information about each software slot and its contents. 9
The following information is provided by software-inventory reply message: 10
a) name - name of the software slot (the name is defined by the O-RU vendor) 11
b) status - status of the software package. Status of the package can be  12
 - VALID - Slot contains a software build considered as proven valid. 13
 - INVALID - software build is not currently used by O-RU. The software is considered by the O-RU as damaged 14
(e.g. wrong CRC). 15
Activation of a software slot containing  an invalid software build shall be prohibited. Note: failed software install 16
operation can cause a slot status to change to "Invalid". 17
 - EMPTY - software slot does not contain a software package. Activation o f an empty software slot shall be 18
prohibited.  19
c) active - indicates if the software stored in particular slot is activated at the moment. 20

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          52
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 - True - software slot contains an activated software build. Active::True can be assigned only for slots with status 1
"Valid". At any time, only one slot in the O-RU MUST be marked as Active::True. The O-RU shall reject activation 2
for software slots with status "Empty" and "Invalid". 3
 - False - software slot contains passive software build or is empty 4
d) running - informs if software stored in particular slot is used at the moment. 5
 - True - software slot contains the software build used by the O-RU in its current run. 6
 - False - software slot contains a software build not used by O-RU at the moment. 7
e) access – informs about access rights for the current slot 8
- READ_ONLY – The slot is intended only for factory software, activation of such software slot means performing 9
a factory reset operation and a return to factory defaults settings. 10
- READ_WRITE – slot used for updating software 11
f) product-code - product code provided by the vendor, specific to the product. 12
g) vendor-code - unique code of the vendor. 13
h) build-id - Identity associated with the software build.  This id is used to find the appropriate build -version for the 14
product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 15
i) build-name - Name of the software build. 16
j) build-version - Version of the software build for the product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 17
k) files – list of files in build 18
l) name – name of one particular file 19
m) version – version of the file 20
n) local-path - complete path of the file on local file system 21
o) integrity - result of the file integrity check 22
- OK – file integrity is correct 23
- NOK – file is corrupted 24
If a slot contains a file with integrity::NOK, the O-RU shall mark the whole slot with status::INVALID. The content of a 25
software-slot is fully under O-RU's management - including removal of the content occupying the slot (in case the slot is subject 26
of software update procedure), control of file system consistency and so on. The slot content shall not be removed until there is 27
a need for new software to be installed.  28
Note: The empty slot parameters shall be as follows 29
name: up to vendor, not empty 30
status: "INVALID" 31
active: False 32
running: False 33
access: READ_WRITE 34
product-code: up to vendor 35
vendor code: up to vendor 36
build-name: null (empty string) 37

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          53
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
build-version: null (empty string) 1
files: empty 2
5.3 Download 3
Pre-condition:  4
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 5
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive download-event notifications. 6
Post-condition: 7
- O-RU downloads all files specified and successfully stores the downloaded files in the O-RU’s file system.  8
 9
Figure 13: Software download call flow 10
Following types of authentications are supported for software-download: 11
a) password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 12

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          54
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
b) certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 1
The software-download rpc is used to trigger the downloading of software to the O-RU. The download shall be performed 2
using sFTP. The rpc specifies the URI of the remote location of the software files.  3
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 4
a) STARTED – software download operation has been started 5
b) FAILED – software download operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message  6
When the O-RU completes the software download or software download fail s, the O-RU shall send NETCONF download-7
event notification with one of the following statuses: 8
a) COMPLETED 9
b) AUTHENTICATION_ERROR -  source available, wrong credentials 10
c) PROTOCOL_ERROR – sFTP protocol error 11
d) FILE_NOT_FOUND -  source not available 12
e) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason  13
f) TIMEOUT -  source available, credentials OK, Operation timed out  (e.g. source becomes unavailable during ongoing 14
operation). 15
The above will be repeated until all files which are required for the O-RU and which belong to the software package have been 16
downloaded to the O-RU. 17
5.4 Install 18
Pre-condition:  19
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 20
- At least one software slot with status active::False and running::False exists in O-RU. 21
- Software Download has been completed successfully and files are available in O-RU. 22
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive install-event notifications. 23
Post-condition: 24
- O-RU software is installed in the specified target software-slot. 25

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          55
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 14 Software install call flow 2
NETCONF software-install rpc is used to install the previously downloaded software (all files provided in the package) to the 3
specified target software-slot on O-RU. This slot must have status active::False and running::False.  4
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 5
a) STARTED – software install operation has been started. 6
b) FAILED – software install operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message. 7
When O-RU completes the software install or software install procedure fails, the O-RU will send NETCONF install-event 8
notification with one of the following statuses: 9
a) COMPLETED - Install procedure is successfully completed. 10
b) FILE_ERROR – operation on the file resulted in in error, disk failure, not enough disk space, incompatible file format 11
c) INTEGRITY_ERROR – file is corrupted  12

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          56
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
d) APPLICATION_ERROR – operation failed due to internal reason 1
When the software install commences, the O-RU shall set the slot status to INVALID. After the install procedure finishes, the 2
O-RU shall change the slot status to its appropriate status. This operation avoids reporting of inaccurate status when the install 3
procedure is in operation or when it is interrupted (e.g., by spurious reset operation). 4
5.5 Activation 5
Pre-condition:  6
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 7
- Software slot to be activated has status VALID. 8
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive activation-event notifications. 9
Post-condition: 10
- O-RU software activates to the version of software-slot. 11
 12

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          57
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 15 Software activation call flow. 2
NETCONF software-activate rpc is used to activate the software. The name of the software -slot is specified in the activate 3
request.  4
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 5

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          58
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
a) STARTED – software activation operation has been started 1
b) FAILED – software activation operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message 2
 3
When the activation is completed , the O-RU shall send the NETCONF activation-event notification with the status  of 4
activation. The following status is returned in the NETCONF activation-event notifications. 5
a) COMPLETED - Activation procedure is successfully completed. O-RU must be restarted via NETCONF reset rpc for the 6
new software to be activated. 7
b) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason 8
Only one software slot can be active at a ny time. Thus, successful software-activate command will set active::True to the slot 9
that was provided in the rpc and automatically will set active::False to the previously active slot. 10
NETCONF reset rpc shall be sent to O-RU to activate to the version of the software -slot. O-RU restarts and performs startup 11
procedure as described in Chapter 3 as regular startup with new software version running.  12
5.6 Software update scenario 13
An example scenario of a successful software update procedure can be as follows: 14
1. NETCONF client performs a software inventory operation and identifies that an inactive and not -running slot for 15
installing software is available so that it can download and install a software package. 16
NOTE: This version of this specification does not distinguish between a software upgrade and a downgrade. 17
2. NETCONF client using the software-download rpc requests the O-RU to download a software package (if the 18
software package contains several files, steps 2-4 need to be performed repeatedly until all files have been downloaded) 19
3. O-RU sends rpc response that download was started 20
4. O-RU finishes downloading the file(s) and reports this by sending the download-event notification 21
5. NETCONF client requests installation of the software using software-install rpc, and provides the slot name where 22
the software needs to be installed along with a list of filenames to be installed (if the software package contains only 23
one file, the list will contain only one entry) 24
6. O-RU sends rpc response that installation was started 25
7. O-RU sets installation slot status to INVALID 26
8. O-RU installs the software and after successful install ation (with checksum control) change s status of the slot to 27
VALID 28
9. O-RU notifies the NETCONF client that the installation is finished using install-event notification 29
10. NETCONF client requests the O-RU to activate the newly installed software using the software-activate rpc 30
11. O-RU sends rpc response that activation was started 31
12. For requested slot, O-RU changes active to True and at the same time sets activate to False on previously active slot 32
13. O-RU notifies NETCONF client about activation finished using the activation-event notification 33
14. NETCONF client restarts the O-RU forcing it to use the newly installed and activated software into use. O-RU restarts 34
as regular startup with new software version running. 35

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          59
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
5.7 Factory Reset  1
O-RU can be reset to the factory default software by activat ing the software -slot containing the factory default software and 2
initiating NETCONF reset rpc. O-RU may clear persistent memory data during factory reset as vendor implementation option. 3
Chapter 6 Configuration Management  4
6.1 Baseline configuration 5
This chapter describes NETCONF standard operation (edit-config/get-config/get) [3] which belongs to the CM in Module  to 6
modify/retrieve any parameters in YANG modules. Examples below use o-ran-hardware as an example YANG module. 7
Two following scenarios are feasible for Configuration Management purposes. 8
- 2 phase (modify/commit) operation using writable running datastore 9
- 3 phase (modify/commit/confirm) operation using candidate datastore. 10
The 2-phase operation performs edit config on running datastore directly and confirm operation is not used. 11
All O-RUs shall support 2 phase operation, with 3 phase operations being optional. 12

6.1.4 Modify Parameters 9
Before an O -RU Controller modifies the configuration (candidate or running) of an O -RU, it shall first lock the target 10
configuration. This prevents other NETCONF clients from changing the shared configuration database until the O -RU 11
Controller releases the lock. If another NETCONF client has already locked the configuration datastore, then the O -RU will 12
respond with a NETCONF error indicating that the requested lock is denied. Note, in such circumstances, the O-RU controller 13
should wait for a period of time before re-attempting to modify the O-RU’s configuration. 14
O-RU Controller is able to modify parameters of the YANG module by using the NETCONF <edit-config> procedure. 15
When supported by an O -RU, the O-RU Controller shall perform any required modify operations ONLY on the candidate 16
configuration datastore before committing the validated configuration to the running configuration datastore. When an O -RU 17
does not support the candidate configuration datastore, the O-RU Controller should take extreme care whenever modifying the 18
running configuration datastore as such will likely impact system operation. 19
Note, validation of the modified configuration is based on: 20
1) basic YANG constraints (e.g., min-elements, range, pattern),  21
2) XPATH based YANG constraints (e.g., leafref, must and when statements), and  22
3) external code which implements YANG constraints (e.g., defined in O -RAN specifications, YANG description 23
statements, etc.). 24
In case of failures, an error will be returned. Please refer to RFC6241 Appendix A for error codes. 25
The vendor can define the behavior after error occurred. 26

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          64
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 25 – Modify Parameters 2
Preconditions: 3
- O-RU Controller has completed exchange of NETCONF capabilities as part of connection establishment between the O-RU 4
and O-RU Controller(s). 5
- O-RU Controller has locked the target configuration 6
Post conditions: 7
- O-RU controller has retrieved O-RU resource state as per <edit-config> request 8
• Success case: The update is confirmed to O-RU Controller. 9
• Failure case: Failure reason is provided to O-RU Controller 10
Sequential processing is assumed.  Only a single <edit -config> rpc is allowed at a time. Next <edit -config> rpc shall be 11
performed after previous <edit-config> rpc reply. 12
Modify Parameters is used to:  13
- update parameters of existing leafs,  14
O-RU shall be allowed to reject <edit -config> in case the content is found to be against e.g. , functions supported by O-RU - 15
like carrier configured out of band. 16
After the modification procedure is complete, the O-RU Controller releases the lock on the target configuration. 17
6.2 Framework for optional feature handling 18
This section describes the common and optional features about Configuration Management. 19
An O-RU may have some features which are not supported by other O-RUs, i.e. optional feature (s). In this case , the O-RU 20
needs to inform the O-RU controller which features the O-RU can provide, and this can be achieved by exchanging NETCONF 21
capabilities. 22

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          65
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Some of the YANG models are optional for the O-RU to support. For example, in this version of the management pl ane 1
specification, those models associated with External IO and Antenna Line Devices are not essential for the operation of the O-2
RAN fronthaul interface. Other mandatory models define optional feature capabilities. 3
The NETCONF Server shall use the ietf-yang-library model (RFC 7895) [20] to list the namespace of the models supported by 4
the Server. If an O-RU/NETCONF server does not return the namespace associated with an optional YANG model, the 5
NETCONF client determines that the O-RU does not support the optional capability associated with the model. 6
In addition, for each supported schema, the ietf-yang-library lists the YANG feature names from this module that are supported 7
by the server. The details of optional models and features are defined in Annex C. 8
6.1.5 Deleting Parameters 9
Before an O -RU Controller deletes any configuration (candidate or running) of an O -RU, it shall first lock the target 10
configuration. This prevents other NETCONF clients from changing the shared configuration database until the O -RU 11
Controller releases the lock. If another NETCONF client has already locked the configuration datastore, then the O -RU will 12
respond with a NETCONF error indicating that the requested lock is denied. Note, in such circumstances, the O-RU controller 13
should wait for a period of time before re-attempting to delete the O-RU’s configuration. 14
O-RU Controller is able to delete parameters of the YANG module by using the NETCONF <edit-config> procedure with the 15
“operation” attribute set to delete. 16
If the configuration data does not exist, an <rpc-error> element is returned with an <error-tag> value of "data-missing". 17
When supported by an O -RU, the O -RU Controller shall perform any required delete operations ONLY on the candidate 18
configuration datastore before committing the validated configuration to the running configuration datastore. When an O -RU 19
does not support the candidate configuration datastore, the O-RU Controller should take extreme care whenever modifying the 20
running configuration datastore as such will likely impact system operation. 21
 22

and O-RU Controller(s). 27

6.3 M-Plane Operational State 11
The o-ran-mplane-int YANG model allows the O-RU to report the connectivity to NETCONF clients on  a per sub -interface 12
level. The client information includes the IP address(es) for the client(s) as well as the link-layer address used to forward packets 13
towards the various management plane clients. 14
6.4 Notification of Updates to Configuration Datastore 15
6.4.1 Introduction 16
This sub-section defines an optional O-RU capability which allows O-RU Controllers to configure the O-RU to provide 17
notifications of modifications to its YANG datastore. This capability can be used when the O-RU is operating in a hybrid 18
environment with multiple simultaneous NETCONF sessions established to different O-RU controllers. Using this capability, 19
one particular O-RU controller uses the NETCONF notifications functionality specified in RFC 6470 [35] to enable it to be 20
automatically signalled changes to the O-RU’s configuration made by a second O-RU controller. Additionally, if the O-RU 21
supports a vendor specific interface to allow manual configuration, this functionality can also be used to signal such 22
configuration modifications to an O-RU Controller. 23
6.4.2 Subscribing to updates from an O-RU 24
When an O-DU receives an indication from an O-RU that it supports the optional capability to support notification of updates 25
to its configuration data store, as a minimum, it shall subscribe to the netconf-config-change notification. 26
An example subscription to the event notification stream is shown in Figure 27, where one O-RU Controller is receiving a 27
notification that the configuration of the O-RU’s timezone offset has been modified by a second O-RU controller.  28

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          67
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 27 – Example of a netconf-config-change notification 2
Chapter 7 Performance Management 3
This chapter provides the description of scenarios related to performance management. It consists of 2 functions. One is for the 4
measurement activation and the other is the collection of measurement results. 5
7.1 Measurement Activation and De-activation 6
The measurement activation at the start-up installation is also allowed as described in chapter 3.  7
Pre-condition:  8
M-Plane is operational.  9
Post-condition: 10
Measurement is activated or deactivated as per NETCONF client’s request. 11
This sub -section provides information about how to activate  and de-activate the performance measurement via NETCONF 12
<edit-config> to O-RU. The performance measurement is defined as o-ran-performance-management YANG module. In case 13
of multiple NETCONF clients, only one NETCONF client shall activate/deactivate the measurements in the O-RU. 14
In the performance-management YANG module, the following parameters are defined. 15
- group of the measurement results, e.g., transceiver-measurement-objects, rx-window-measurement-objects, tx-16
measurement-objects and epe-measurement-objects. 17
- measurement-interval: measurement interval for the measurement-objects to measure the performance periodically, 18
e.g., 300, 600, 900 seconds. It is defined per the group of the measurement result. 19
- measurement-object: target metric to measure the performance, e.g., RX_POWER, TX_POWER , defined  as key 20
parameter. 21
- active: enable/disable the performance measurement per measurement-object. This va lue is Boolean.  Default is 22
FALSE. 23
- start-time and end-time: to report the time of measurement start and end for the measurement-object at each 24
measurement-interval. 25
- object-unit: unit to measure the performance per object, e.g., O-RU, physical port number, antenna, carrier. The object-26
unit may be configurable  Identifier object-unit-id means e.g., physical port number when object unit set to physical 27
port number. 28
<notification xmlns="urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:netconf:notification:1.0">
  <eventTime>2020-03-01T08:00:14.12Z</eventTime>
  <netconf-config-change xmlns= "urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:yang:ietf-netconf-
notifications">
    <id>102</id>
    <changed-by>
      <username>nms-user</username>
      <session-id>1099</session-id>
      <source-host>10.10.10.10</source-host>
    </changed-by>
    <datastore>running</datastore>
    <edit>
      <target>/oran-ops:operational-info/oran-ops:clock/oran-
ops:timezoneutc-offset</target>
      <operation>replace</operation>
    </edit>
  </netconf-config-change>
</notification>

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          68
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
- report-info: th e reporting info to the measurement-object, e.g., MAXIMUM, MINIMUM, FIRST, LATEST, 1
FREQUENCY_TABLE and COUNT. Multiple info can be considered for one object if necessary. 2
- Optional configurable parameter(s) for report-info: some configurable parameters to report, e.g., function, bin-count, 3
upper-bound, lower-bound. For the bin-count configuration, it shall be less than the parameter max-bin-count that is 4
the capability information of NETCONF server for the maximum configurable value for bin-count. 5
- Additional reporting information for report-info: some additional information to report info, e.g., date-and-time. 6
 7
The detail of the parameters per measurement-object and the group of measurement result are defined in Annex B. 8
The measurement-interval of measurement-object may be set to common or different values per group of the measurement 9
result.  10
It is allowed that the measurement is activated and deactivated at any time. When different parameter measurements have 11
intervals with a common factor, the O-RU shall synchronize the boundary of these measurements aligned with this factor, 12
irrespective of when the different measurements are activated. And all of start point s of the measurement-intervals shall be 13
synchronized to zero o’clock mid-night by using an equation {full seconds (hour, minute and second) modulo ‘measurement-14
interval’ = 0}, in order to ensure the same start and end of the measurement-intervals between O-RUs. For more detail see 15
the following illustration. 16
 17
Figure 28: synchronization of measurement-interval. 18
 19
The modification of the configurable parameters for the measurement shall be allowed  while active for the corresponding 20
measurement-object is set to FALSE. 21
All of the measurements are optionally supported in the O-RU.  22
The report-info, e.g., count, shall be started from 0 at the boundary of every measurement-interval. No accumulation is 23
applied between the measurement-intervals. 24
 7.2 Collection and Reporting of Measurement Result 25
This sub-section provides the description of scenarios used to collect measurement results. There are three options. 26
1. NETCONF process: Create-subscription from NETCONF client and NETCONF notification from NETCONF server 27
are used. 28
2. File Management process: File upload mechanism is used for the measurement file from O-RU to configured file 29
server(s) that O-RU can reach to. 30
3. Configured subscription process: Create configured subscription from O-RU as Event-Producer to Event-Collector. 31

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          69
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Methods 1 and 2 are mandatory for the O-RU. Method 3 shall be supported by those O -RUs that support the optional NON-1
PERSISTENT-MPLANE feature. The method(s) to be used is the matter of NETCONF client. 2
In case of multiple NETCONF clients and/or Event-Collectors, the O-RU shall report the same notification-based measurement 3
results to all subscribed NETCONF clients /Event-Collectors, and the O-RU shall upload file-based results to all configured 4
fileservers. 5
7.2.1 NETCONF process 6
This process needs the NETCONF capability: urn:ietf:params:netconf:capability:notification:1.0 7
1. NETCONF client subscribes to one or more measurement  group(s) and/or measurement-object(s) to collect the 8
measurement result by sending NETCONF <subscribe-notification> to NETCONF server in the O-RU. In this message, 9
startTime and stopTime for the notification may be configurable. NETCONF client can configure the notification-interval 10
in the performance-measurement YANG module.  11
2.  NETCONF server sends NETCONF notification  messages periodically to the client as configured by  the notification-12
interval. The NETCONF notification message contains subscribed measurement group(s) and/or measurement-object(s). 13
The notification-interval doesn’t need to be same as the measurement-interval. The notification timing different from the 14
measurement-interval is a matter to O-RU implementation. 15
This procedure is described in the following figure. 16
 17
Figure 29: NETCONF process of Measurement Result Collection 18
Note: This figure uses create-subscription for the single stream " measurement-result-stats". In order to subscribe multiple 19
notifications, the appropriate create-subscription message is required. Please refer to section 8.2 for the appropriate example 20
of create-subscription of multiple notifications. 21
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall send <close-session> operation from the subscription session. 22
If NETCONF session is terminated by <kill-session>, the subscribed notification is terminated as well.  23
This procedure is described in the following figure. 24

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 30: NETCONF process of Measurement Result Collection to end 2
When notification-interval is larger than measurement-interval, one notification may contain multiple stats which have 3
consecutive periods indicating start-time and end-time for the measurement. 4
When notification-interval is smaller than measurement-interval, one notification may not contain the stats which start-time 5
and end-time are not applicable to the period for the notification. 6
For example, when notification-interval = 60min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 7
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one n otification contains 2 measurement results for 8
measurement-object#A with consecutive start-time and end-time, and 4 measurement results for measurement-object#B 9
with consecutive start-time and end-time.  10
For the other example, when notification-interval = 15min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 11
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains one measurement results for 12
measurement-object#B but not for measurement-object#A. next notification contains b oth measurements result for 13
measurement-object#A and #B. 14
7.2.2 File Management process 15
NETCONF client needs to configure a parameter of performance measurement YANG module ‘enable-SFTP-upload’ to 16
enable or disable the periodic file upload mechanism via NETCONF <edit-config>. Its default is FALSE. 17
In addition, t he performance measurement YANG module defines file-upload-interval, remote-SFTP-upload-path, 18
credentials information of the file server and enable-random-file-upload as configurable parameters. 19
Following types of authentications are supported for performance file upload: 20
a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 21
b) Certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 22
When the parameter enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE, O-RU shall store the performance measurement files in the generic 23
folder in O-RU, i.e., O-RAN/PM/. Every file-upload-interval, O-RU pushes the latest file to upload to the  remote-SFTP-24
upload-path of the configured SFTP servers if enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE. Otherwise, the performance measurement 25
file is not created and uploaded. The number of maximum performance files to be stored in O-RU simultaneously is a matter 26
for O-RU implementation. The O-RU shall manage its own storage space by deleting the older files autonomously.  27
The O-RU shall ensure that the start-time and the  end-time within the name of the performance measurement file are 28
synchronized with the same manner as measurement-interval by using file-upload-interval. 29

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          71
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
If the parameter enable-random-file-upload is set to TRUE, the O-RU shall randomize the timing to upload SFTP file after 1
the performance measurement file is ready to upload. The randomized timing is an O-RU implementation matter and shall not 2
be later than next file-upload-interval. 3
The file name of the performance measurement is: 4
C<start-time>_<end-time>_<name>.csv 5
- Starting with a capital letter “C”. 6
- Format of <start-time> and <end-time> can be local time or UTC. 7
Local time format is YYYYMMDDHHMM+HHMM, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute, timezone “+” or “ -“, 8
hour and minute for the time zone. 9
UTC format is YYYYMMDDHHMMZ, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute and with a special UTC designator 10
("Z")   11
Time zone offset is provided by timezone-utc-offset in o-ran-operation.yang. 12
- <name> in ietf-hardware is used  13
- “_” underscore is located between <start-time>, <end-time> and <name> 14
- File extension is “csv” as csv format file. 15
Example of measurement file is: 16
C201805181300+0900_201805181330+0900_ABC0123456.csv. 17
 18
The file format of the performance measurement has following rule: 19
1. Each line starts with the measurement-object identifier, which measurement can be switched to TRUE or FALSE by 20
active parameter. The identifier of each measurement-object is defined in Annex B. 21
2. After the measurement-object identifier, the name of measurement-object, start-time, end-time are followed. 22
3. Since the report-info results of any measurement-object are measured per object-unit, object-unit-id and set of report-23
info are repeated in one line. 24
4. When multiple report-info parameters exist per object-unit, all of the report-info are consecutively listed until the next 25
object-unit-id. The order of parameters, such as object-unit-id, report-info and additional information for the report-info, 26
shall be same as the order of those listed in NETCONF notification defined in o-ran-performance-management YANG 27
module. 28
Example of measurement result in one line is: 29
1, RX_ON_TIME, 2018 -05-18T13:00:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00, 0, 123, AAAA , 1, 123, BBBB, 2, 123, CCCC, 3, 123, 30
DDDD 31
- Measurement-object-identifier: 1 32
- Name of measurement-object: RX_ON_TIME 33
- start-time: 2018-05-18T13:00:00+09:00 as measurement start-time. 34
- end-time: 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00 as measurement end-time 35
- EAXC_ID: 0 36
- Count for EAXC_ID#0 : 123 37
- name of transport-flow information:  AAAA 38
- : 39

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          72
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
- EAXC_ID: 3 1
- Count for EAXC_ID#3 : 123 2
- name of transport-flow information:  DDDD 3
When file-upload-interval is larger than measurement-interval, one performance measurement file may contain multiple 4
lines for the stats which have consecutive periods indicating start-time and end-time for the measurement. 5
When file-upload-interval is smaller than measurement-interval, one performance measurement file may not contain the line 6
for the stats which start-time and end-time are not applicable to the period for the performance measurement file. 7
For example, when  file-upload-interval = 60min,  measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 8
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one performance measurement file  contains 2 measurement 9
result lines for measurement-object#A with consecutive  start-time and end-time, and 4 measurement result lines for  10

1, RX_POWER, 2018-05-18T13:00:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:15:00+09:00, 0, 123 12
1, RX_POWER, 2018-05-18T13:15:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00, 0, 123 13

DDDD  15
1, RX_POWER, 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:45:00+09:00, 0, 123 16
1, RX_POWER, 2018-05-18T13:45:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T14:00:00+09:00, 0, 123 17

DDDD 19
For the other example, when file-upload-interval = 15min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 20
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one performance measurement file contains one measurement 21
result line for measurement-object#B but not for measurement-object#A. next performance measurement file contains both 22
measurements result for measurement-object#A and #B as follows. 23
C201805181300Z+0900_201805181315+0900_ABC0123456.csv. 24
1, RX_POWER, 2018-05-18T13:00:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:15:00+09:00, 0, 123 25

The performance measurement files stored in O-RAN/PM can be uploaded on-demand. For the file upload mechanism by on-30
demand way, retrieve-file-list and file-upload operations are used. For more detail, please refer to Chapter 9. 31
7.2.3 Configured Subscription Process 32
This optional process requires the O-RU to support configured subscriptions, as described in Chapter 15. The structure of the 33
process follows the NETCONF process described in sub -section 7.2.1. However, instead of sending a NETCONF <create -34
subscription > to the NETCONF server in the O-RU to subscribe to the measurement-result-stats notifications, the NETCONF 35
client installs the subscription via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends 36
asynchronous YANG notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-Collector. 37
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall delete the corresponding configuration in the O -RU. 38
Immediately after the subscription is successfully deleted, the O -RU will send to a subscription state change notification 39
indicating that the subscription has ended to the Event-Collector.  40
Note, unlike the NETCONF process described in section 7.2.1, the subscription to the subscribed notifications is not terminated 41
when the NETCONF session used to establish the subscription is terminated.  42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          73

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Chapter 8 Fault Management 1
Fault management is responsible for  sending alarm notifications to the configured subscriber, which will typically be the 2
NETCONF Client  unless the O -RU supports the configured subscription capability, as described in Chapter 15, when the 3
configured subscriber may be an Event-Collector. FM contains Fault Management Managed Element and via this Managed 4
Element alarm notifications can be disabled or enabled. 5
The NETCONF Server is responsible for managing an “active -alarm-list”. Alarms with severity “warning” are excluded from 6
this list. When an alarm is detected it is added to the list; when the alarm reason disappears then the alarm is cleared - removed 7
from the “active-alarm-list”. Furthermore, when the element that was the “fault -source” of an alarm is deleted then all related 8
alarms are removed from the “active-alarm-list”. 9
The NETCONF Client can read “active-alarm-list” by get rpc operation. 10
 11
Figure 31: Read Active Alarms 12
8.1 Alarm Notification 13
The O-RU is responsible to send <alarm -notif> to a configured subscriber  when the NETCONF Client has established a 14
subscription to alarm notification and: 15
- a new alarm is detected (this can be the same alarm as an already existing one, but reported against a different “fault-source” 16
than the existing alarm)  17
- an alarm is removed from the list   18
Removal of alarms from the list due to deletion of “fault-source” element is considered as clearing and cause sending of <alarm-19
notif> to the configured subscriber. This applies to alarms which were explicitly related to the deleted “fault -source” element. 20
The rationale for such is to avoid misalignment between NETCONF Clients when one NETCONF Client deletes an element.  21
The O-RU reports in <alarm-notif> only for new active or cancelled alarms, not all active alarms. 22

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          74
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00

8.3 Fault Sources 7
Alarm notifications reported by NETCONF Server contain element “fault -source” which indicates the origin of an alarm. In 8
general values of “fault-source” are based on names defined as YANG leafs: 9
- Source (Examples: fan, module, PA, port) 10
indicates that origin of the alarm within the O-RU. Value of “fault-source” is based on element name. 11

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          77
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Note: In case the NETCONF Server reports an unknown “fault-source”, the NETCONF Client can discard the <alarm-1
notif>. 2
- Source (other than when an element is within the O-RU) 3
Value of fault-source may be empty or may identify the most likely external candidate; for example, antenna line.   4
 5
Alarms with different “fault-id”, “fault-source” or "fault-severity" are independent: 6
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-id” may be reported with different “fault-source”.  7
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-source” may be reported with different “fault-id”.  8
- When an alarm with a "fault -id" and a "fault-source" is reported with a "fault -severity" and its severity of alarm condition 9
is upgraded or degraded, NETCONF server reports a new alarm with the same "fault -id" and the same "fault-source" with 10
the upgraded or degraded "fault -severity" with "is-cleared"::FALSE and clears the previous alarm with the report of the 11
"fault-id", "fault-source" and "fault-severity" with "is-cleared":: TRUE.  12
The range of "fault-id" is separated to common and vendor specific. The common fault -ids are defined in Annex A and more 13
number will be used in future. The vendor specific range for the fault-id shall be [1000 .. 65535]. 14
Alarm notifications reported by the NETCONF Server contain names of the “affected-objects” which indicate elements affected 15
by the fault. In case the origin of the alarm is within the O-RU, other elements than “fault-source” which will not work correctly 16
due to the alarm are reported via “affected -objects”. In case the origin of the fault is outside of the O-RU, the O-RU elements 17
which will not work correctly due to the fault are reported via “affected-objects”. 18
8.4 Manage Alarms Request to Event-Collector 19
This optional capability requires the O-RU to support configured subscriptions, as described in Chapter 15. The structure of the 20
process follows the process described in sub -section 8.2. However, instead of sending a NETCONF <create -subscription> to 21
the NETCONF server in the O-RU to subscribe to the alarm-notif notifications, the NETCONF client installs the subscription 22
via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends asynchronous YANG 23
notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-Collector. 24
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall delete the correspon ding configuration in the O -RU. 25
Immediately after the subscription is successfully deleted, the O -RU will send to a subscription state change notification 26
indicating that the subscription has ended to the Event-Collector.  27
Chapter 9 File Management 28
This chapter specifies File Management for the O-RU. Following operations are supported as a File Management. 29
- upload (see subsection 9.2) 30
 File upload from O-RU to file server triggered by O-RU Controller. 31
- retrieve file list (see subsection 9.3) 32
 O-RU Controller retrieves the file list in O-RU. 33
- download (see subsection 9.4) 34
 File download from file server to O-RU triggered by O-RU Controller 35
Note: file-download has different purpose with software-download specified in subsection 5.3. For example, file-download 36
can be used for Beamforming configuration in subsection 12.4. 37
File transfers are done with sFTP. Following types of authentications are supported for file management: 38
a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 39

b) Certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 1
Following other sections are related with File Management. 2
