The O-RU exposes its ability to support TDD pattern configuration by support of the feature CONFIGURABLE-TDD-43
PATTERN-SUPPORTED in o-ran-module-cap.yang module. Presence of this feature means, that at least one of static-44
low-level-[tr]x-endpoints offered by the O-RU supports configuration for TDD pattern , so that these static-low-level-45

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        129
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
[tr]x-endpoints can be used (through low-level-[tr]x-endpoints) by [tr]x-array-carriers having configurable TDD pattern 1
assigned.  2
Note: Configured TDD pattern shall not be violated by C-Plane and U-Plane messages. 3
Note: In case configuration provided to O-RU contains records for TDD pattern(s), PRACH patterns and/or SRS 4
patterns, O-RU validates consistency between patterns. Configuration where there is collision between patterns 5
detected, shall be rejected by O-RU. 6
From the model perspective, configuration for TDD pattern is supported by static -low-level-[tr]x-endpoints having 7
parameter configurable-tdd-pattern exposed as TRUE. Suc h static -low-level-[tr]x-endpoint can be respectively 8
referenced by low -level-[tr]x-endpoint designated to serve for [tr]x-array-carrier having preconfigured TDD pattern 9
assigned. Specific configuration of the TDD pattern may be utilised by [tr]x -array-carrier according to the optional 10
parameter configurable-tdd-pattern.  11
Absence of leaf configurable-tdd-pattern at [tr]x-array-carrier means, that such [tr]x-array-carrier has no configurable-12
tdd-pattern assigned. 13
A configurable TDD pattern can be assigned to  a [tr]x-array-carrier under the condition, that all static -low-level-[tr]x-14
endpoints serving such an [tr]x-array-carrier expose value of capability configurable-tdd-pattern-supported as TRUE. 15
A s ingle [tr]x -array-carrier can only  reference to single insta nce of configurable -tdd-pattern. Whereas, a s ingle 16
configurable-tdd-pattern shall be referenced by all cooperating [tr]x -array-carriers serving for a specific [tr]x-array. 17
Linkage between tx -array-carriers and rx -array-carriers configured to use the same c onfigurable-tdd-pattern must be 18
assured by the entity responsible for configuration provisioning to O-RU. For example, ensuring that all cooperating [tr]x-19
array-carriers use static -low-level-[tr]x-endpoints (through low -level-[tr]x-endpoints) having the sa me value of tdd-20
group. The practical implication of this is that static-low-level-[tr]x-endpoints exposing the same value of parameter tdd-21
group must be used by low -level-[tr]x-endpoints serving for [tr]x-array-carriers having the same TDD switching points 22
and the same directions to the air interface granted by TDD patterns they are configured to use. 23
Note: M-Plane model allows an O-RU to be configured with more than one TDD patterns. This is capability can 24
be used by O-RUs having more than one [tr]x-array. 25
A single TDD pattern configuration consists of list of records. Each single record contains details for frame-offset and 26
direction of signal that must be applied at the moment a specific frame-offset occurs at air interface. Supported 27
directions are UL (uplink), DL (downlink) and GP (neither uplink nor downlink). 28
Note: Assignment of configurable-tdd-pattern to a [tr]x-array-carrier is only possible in case all following 29
conditionals are met: 30
- O-RU supports feature CONFIGURABLE-TDD-PATTERN-SUPPORTED. 31
- all static-low-level-[tr]x-endpoint configured to serve for a specific [tr]x-array-carrier have capability 32
configurable-tdd-pattern set to TRUE 33

Chapter 13 Licensed-Assisted Access 1
13.1 Introduction: 2
Licensed-assisted access (LAA) leverages the carrier -aggregation (CA) functionality. With LAA, CA is performed 3
between licensed and unlicensed component carriers (CCs). This enables the LAA system to opportunistically benefit 4
from using unlicensed spectrum (e.g., UNII bands in the 5 GHz spectrum) to enhance the aggregated capacity of the O -5
RU with the objective of enhancing the downlink throughput. 6
Several modifications in the RAN are needed to enable LAA in the O -DU and O-RU such as listen -before-talk (LBT), 7
discontinuous transmission, carrier-selection, discovery reference signal (DRS) transmission, etc. This section is focused 8
on the LAA -related messages and procedures needed in the M -plane. The C -plane related messages are defined in the 9
CUS-plane spec [2]. 10
This version of the M -plane spec supports only LAA based on Rel. 13 of the 3GPP specs, where transmission on the 11
unlicensed spectrum can be done only in the downlink direction. The support of eLAA Rel. 14 (i.e., enabling UL 12
transmission on the unlicensed spectrum) may be included in a later version of the M-plane spec.  13
The modifications at M-plane to Support LAA can be summarized as follows: 14
i) LAA-initiation process: O-DU learns about O-RU capabilities and configures it.  15
• O-RU LAA Support: The O -RU indicates it supports LAA by including support for the "urn:o -16
ran:laa:x.y" and "urn:o -ran:laa-operations:x.y" namespaces in its ietf -yang-library model (RFC 7895) 17
[20]. 18
• O-RU LAA Capability Information: When the LAA feature is enabled, leafs corresponding to LAA -19
related O-RU capabilities, such as the number of supported LAA SCarriers, maximum LAA buffer size, 20
etc, are conveyed via the M-plane to the O-DU as part of the o-ran-module-cap.yang module.  21
• O-RU LAA Configuration: The NETCONF client configures the unlicensed LAA component carrier 22
with the LAA -related parameters such as the energy -detection threshold, DRS measurement t iming 23
configuration (DMTC) period, etc. as part of the o -ran-uplane-config.yang module. The configuration 24
of the number of LAA SCarriers, multi-carrier type, etc. is performed using the o-ran-laa.yang Module. 25
• For explanation of the LAA -initiation process, please refer to Figure 4 in Chapter 3, where the O -RU 26
LAA capability info is conveyed within the “Retrieval of O-RU information” step, while the O-RU LAA 27
configurations are conveyed in “Configuring the O-RU operational parameters” step in Figure 4.  28
ii) Carrier-selection: Selecting the best channel in the unlicensed band, both initially and dynamically over time.  29
 30

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        131
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00

13.2 LAA-initiation Process   3
13.2.1 LAA Module Capabilities 4
During LAA-initiation, the O-RU reports its LAA capabilities to the NETCONF client. These capabilities are sent at the 5
start up as part of the o-ran-module-cap.yang module. The attributes included are: 6
(1) sub-band-frequency-ranges: The unlicensed sub -bands (e.g., 46A, 46B, etc.) that are supported at the O -RU and 7
their frequency ranges 8

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        132
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
(2) number-of-laa-scarriers (uint8): Number of LAA SCarriers that the O-RU can support.  1
(3) maximum-laa-buffer-size (uint16): Maximum O-RU buffer size in Kilobytes (KB) per CC. This parameter is needed 2
at the O-DU to know how much data can be sent in advance and stored at the O-RU to address the LBT uncertainty.  3
(4) maximum-processing-time (uint16): Maximum O-RU Processing time in microseconds at the O -RU to handle the 4
received/transmitted packets from/to the O -DU. This parameter is needed at the O -DU to determine the time where it 5
needs to send the data to the O-RU.  6
 (5) self-configure (Boolean): Capability to manage the contention window at the O-RU. Based on the CUS-spec, there 7
are two modes of operation for LAA, 1) when the contention window is managed by the O-DU, and 2) when the 8
contention window is managed by the O-RU. This field is set to True if the O-RU can manage the contention window 9
locally.  10
13.2.2 LAA O-RU Parameter Configuration 11
The second stage of the LAA -initiation process is the configuration message (using RPC edit -config). In this message, 12
the O -DU configures the O -RU with the required parameters in the downlink direction. LAA parameters can be 13
configured by Netconf Client after capability exchange is finished. It can also be sent as needed, to reconfigure the O-RU 14
with new parameters (e.g., ed-threshold-pdsch, etc.). The attributes of this message (o-ran-laa.yang Module) include: 15
(1) number-of-laa-scarriers (uint8): Number of LAA SCarriers to be used at the O-RU. This number should be less 16
than or equal the number reported by the O-RU in its module capabilities.  17
(2) multi-carrier-type (Enumeration): This value indicates the list of multi carrier types (A1, A2, B1, B2) which as 18
subsection 15.1.5 in [32].  19
(3) multi-carrier-tx (Boolean): This value indicates whether self-deferral is activated or not. “True” indicates 20
transmission on channel access win (i.e., no self-deferral). “False” indicates mutual transmission on multiple carriers. 21
(4) multi-carrier-freeze (Boolean): This value indicates if the absence of other technology in the unlicensed band can 22
be guaranteed. This attribute can only be used when the multi-carrier-type is A1. “False” indicates that absence of other 23
technology is not guaranteed. 24
(5) laa-ending-dwpts-supported (Boolean): This value indicates whether LAA ending in Downlink Pilot Time Slot 25
(DwPTS) is supported. 26
(6) laa-starting-in-second-slot-supported (Boolean): This value indicates LAA starting in second slot is supported. 27
LAA carrier configurations (o-ran-uplane-conf.yang Module) include:  28
(1) ed-threshold-pdsch (int8): This value indicates the energy detection (ED) threshold for LBT for PDSCH and for 29
measurements in dBm. 30
(2) ed-threshold-drs (int8): This value indicates the ED threshold for LBT for DRS in dBm. 31
 (4) tx-antenna-ports (uint8): This value indicates the Tx antenna ports for DRS.  32
(5) transmission-power-for-drs (int8): This value indicates the offset of CRS power to reference signal power (dB). 33
(6) dmtc-period (enumeration): This value indicates DMTC period in milliseconds.  34
(7) dmtc-offset (uint8): This value indicates DMTC offset in Subframes. 35
(8) lbt-timer (uint16): This value indicates LBT Timer in milliseconds. 36
If Self Configure capability is set to “true”, the following parameters are also needed to be configured. For every traffic 37
priority class, the O -DU needs to configure maximum CW usage counter. Thi s value indicates the maximum value of 38
counter which shows how many max congestion window value is used for back off number of each priority class traffic. 39
This value is defined at section 15.1.3 of [32] as K. Based on the 3GPP specification, this value is selected by O-RU from 40
the set of values {1, 2, …, 8} 41

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        133
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
13.3 Carrier-Selection  1
13.3.1 LAA Measurements 2
The function of the message “ rpc start-measurements” is to order the O -RU to start measurements. This message can 3
be used for carrier selection initially or dynamically over time. O -RU sends RPC response where status==ACCEPTED 4
(positive case) or REJECTED (negative case). O -RU performs measurement and delivers result with respect to max 5
response time. If result is not ready on time - O-RU sends notification with "measurement-success" == FALSE and with 6
appropriate failure reason. For every configured band, the O-RU informs the NETCONF client whether the measurement 7
was successful or not. For bands with successful measurements, the O-RU reports the occupancy ratio and average RSSI 8
for each channel. For bands with failure measurements, the O -RU includes the reason (e.g., TIMEOUT when the O -RU 9
is not able to finish the measurement for this specific band).  10
The occupancy ratio of a given channel is defined as the p ercentage of the busy duration (i.e., measured signal power is 11
larger than the energy -detection threshold) to the total measurement duration of this specific channel. The energy -12
detection threshold is specified in the o -ran-uplan-conf.yang module using the  ed-threshold-pdsch leaf. Note that this 13
threshold is the same as the energy -detection threshold used for LBT for PDSCH transmission. The total measurement 14
duration per channel is specified in o -ran-laa-operation module using the duration-per-channel leaf. The range of the 15
occupancy ratio is from 0% (no signal is detected over the total measurement duration per channel) to 100% (i.e., channel 16
was always occupied during measurement).  17
The average RSSI of the measured channel is the measured power of this spe cific channel averaged over the total 18
measurement duration per channel. This parameter is reported to the NETCONF client in dBm and takes a value from the 19
range 0 dBm to -128 dBm. 20
13.3.2 LAA Carrier Frequency Configuration 21
After receiving the measurements,  the NETCONF client configures the O -RU with the new channel(s), if needed. For 22
every component carrier (CC) that needs to be configured with a new center frequency, the O -DU will need to first 23
deactivate the TX carrier, delete it, then create a new TX car rier (with the new center carrier frequency as well as any 24
other new configurations), and then activate the TX carrier again to start OTA operation. The procedure for 25
deactivating/deleting/creating/activating the carrier is explained in Section 12.3: Carri er Configuration, in the M -plane 26
specification and elaborated in Figure 50. Note that the creation of LAA carriers is identical to the creation of regular 27
carriers but in the unlicensed bands. O-RU responds to the configuration request with success or failure.  28
Note also that carrier -selection algorithm at the O -DU (i.e., selecting the “best” channel based on the reported 29
measurements from the O-RU) is an implementation issue and is out of the scope of this document. 30
Chapter 14 Shared Cell 31
This chapter specifies the support of the “Shared Cell” O-RU use case. The features of C/U-Plane aspects are described 32
in chapter 11 of [2]. The M-Plane aspects necessary to support Shared Cell are described in this chapter. 33
14.1 Architecture 34
The NETCONF client (O-RU Controller) establishes M-Plane connection individually to each O-RU, where the O-RUs 35
are operating in either cascade mode or FHM mode Figure 69. In this figure, solid lines indicate C/U-plane interface and 36
dotted lines indicate M-plane interface. Therefore, from the M -Plane point of view, the same architecture model can be 37
applied as specified in Chapter 2.1.2. New functionality which is required to be added, together with existing functionality 38
which is required to be enhanced are specified in sub -sections 14.2 to 14.5. There are no changes to the functionality 39
described in the following chapters and their associated YANG models:   40
- Chapter 5 : Software Management 41
- Chapter 8 : Fault Management 42
- Chapter 9 : File Management 43
 44

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        134
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
A NETCONF client with suitable privileges is able to trigger a reset procedure for each O-RU. It is strongly recommended 1
that when triggering the reset procedures for multiple O -RUs, a NETCONF client should order the procedures such that 2
a reset of an individual O -RU does not affect th e operation of other O -RUs operating in either cascade or FHM mode.  3
This can be achieved by correct ordering of the triggering of the reset procedure between the different O-RUs. For example, 4
when triggering a reset involving multiple O-RUs operating in cascade mode, the ordering of the reset trigger sent by the 5
NETCONF client should be done beginning with the last (most -southern) O-RU to the first (most northern) O -RU in 6
chain. In configuration where FHM is used - when FHM reset is needed, O-RUs connected through this FHM should be 7
reset first, then FHM reset can be performed. It is strongly recommended to disable carriers affected by such a reset 8
procedure prior to the triggering of the reset to minimize the impact on C/U-plane traffic as much as possible. In case an 9
O-RU connected through FHM requires to be reset - the reset will not impact to other O-RUs. 10
Note: there is no difference between Hierarchical M -plane architecture and Hybrid M -plane architecture from the 11
point of reset ordering in either cascade mode (chain topology), or FHM mode (star topology). 12
Using this approach, a NETCONF client can performs software management on multiple O -RUs. Since this procedure 13
may require the reset of the O -RU to update the appropriate software file(s) for the O -RUs, the NETCONF client is 14
recommended to order the software management procedures such that the reset procedure issued against one O-RU shall 15
not impact the other O-RUs or FHM. 16
 17
Figure 69: M-Plane Connection 18
14.2 Start-up and Installation 19
This sub-section provides the consideration regarding the shared cell specific additional mechanism for the overall start-20
up mechanism for "O-RUs with Copy and Combine function" and for "O-RUs without Copy and Combine function". 21

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        135
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Each O-RU establishes M-Plane connection individually to the NETCONF client in the O-RU Controller. The procedures 1
through Transport Layer initialization (DHCP process and VLAN scanning) and supervision of NETCONF connection 2
are the same as the Figure 4 in Chapter 3 for both "O-RUs with Copy and Combine function" and "O-RUs without Copy 3
and Combine function".  4

14.3 Performance Management 3

14.3.1 Measurement-group 5
transceiver-stats: 6
O-RU (Cascade / FHM) has multiple connections to O -DU and O -RU (Cascade/Normal). The baseline O -RU models 7
permit O-RUs to be defined with multiple ports and multiple transceiver modules. Transceiver module is defined by o -8
ran-transceiver which refers the port -number for t hese interfaces. Please refer to sub -section 14.5.1 O -RU Information 9
for Shared Cell. In this case, the O-RU (Cascade / FHM) shall be able to report transceiver-stats per port-number. 10
Rx-window-stats: 11
O-RU (Cascade / FHM) shall monitor rx-window-stats per eaxc-id, per transport or per hardware component (O -RU) 12
because it receives data flow from the north-node. 13
Note: This version of the specification does support rx-window-stats to monitor the downlink reception window and 14
doesn’t support monitoring by an O-RU of the uplink traffic from south-node. 15
Tx-stats: 16
O-RU (Cascade / FHM) shall monitor tx-stats per eaxc-id, per transport or per hardware component (O -RU) because it 17
transmits data flow to the north-node. 18
Note: This version of the specification does support tx-stats to monitor uplink traffic and doesn’t support monitoring by 19
an O-RU of the downlink traffic to south-node. 20

14.4 Delay Management 6
In the shared cell environment, the use of O-RU Adaptive Delay capability is not permitted. The O-DU and each O-RU 7
have their own delay parameters and supported transmission window and reception window. Also, the topology of the 8
O-RU configuration can be detected by the topology discovery procedure.  9
The O-DU can determine the delay budget between itself and the O-RUs considering the O-RUs’ topology and delay 10
parameters and its own transmission window and reception window. During this discovery, the required processing time 11
of the O-RU is also considered. The O-RU processing time includes the copy operation for downlink operation, and the 12
combine operation for uplink operation, and the delay periods for the copy and combine operations are defined as t-13
copy and t-combine in o-ran-shared-cell.yang module: 14
t-copy: Corresponding to the maximum FHM or cascade O-RU processing delay between receiving an IQ sample 15
over the fronthaul interface from the north-node, coping it and transmitting it over the fronthaul interface to the 16
south-node. 17
t-combine: Corresponding to the maximum FHM or cascade O-RU processing delay between receiving an IQ sample 18
over the fronthaul interface from the south-node(s), combing them and transmitting it over the fronthaul interface to 19
the north-node. 20
Therefore, based on the above information, the O-DU can determine how many O-RUs are configured to operate in a 21
shared cell instance. 22
After the delay budget between the O-DU and the furthest (southern-most) O-RU in the chain is determined, multiple 23
O-RUs can be configured to operate in between the O-DU and the furthest O-RU. The time budget between the O-DU 24
and the furthest O-RU is constant and is shared for all O-RUs operating in cascade mode.  25
For combine function operation, the O-RU shall await the successful reception of the eCPRI frame(s) from the south-26
node(s). Once the FHM receives the eCPRI frame from all of the south-nodes, the O-RU (FHM) can perform the 27
combine operation. Once the cascade O-RU receives the eCPRI frame from the south-node, the O-RU can perform the 28
combine operation using the eCPRI frame and received radio information. The maximum time an O-RU is permitted to 29
wait for the required eCPRI frames is set by the ta3-prime-max configured by NETCONF client. If the O-RU cannot 30
commence the combination procedure until a time after the configured ta3-prime-max minus static t-combine, e.g., 31
due to the delayed reception of eCPRI frame(s), the O-RU shall discard the delayed eCPRI frames if received and 32
combine other received frames (for FHM mode) or radio information (for Cascade mode). The configurable ta3-prime-33
max shall be equal to or less than ta3-prime-max-upper-limit which is the capability of O-RU, related to the internal 34
memory for combine operation. The detail for C/U-plane aspects is described in chapter 11.3 of [2]. 35
 36
ta3-prime-max: The latest time that FHM or cascade O-RU is allowed to send UL U-plane message to north-node 37
relative to reception timing at O-RU antenna. 38
ta3-prime-max-upper-limit: The upper limit for the configurable ta3-prime-max value. This is the capability 39
information of O-RU that comes from the O-RU internal memory for the combine operation. 40

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        141
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
14.5 Details of O-RU operations for shared cell 1
This sub-section provides the function detail of O-RU operations for a shared cell. 2
14.5.1 O-RU Information for Shared Cell 3
Interfaces to south-node of O-RU with Copy and Combine function 4
Cascade O-RU has one additional transport interface to south-node and FHM has more than one additional transport 5
interfaces to south-nodes, illustrated below. 6
 7
Figure 75: Transport Interfaces of both side of O-RU 8
Both the interface to north-node and the interface to south-node can be defined by ietf-interface YANG model with 9
type = ethernetCsmacd, augmented by o-ran-interface for mac-address and port-number. Transceiver module is 10
defined by o-ran-transceiver which refers the port-number for these interfaces. The maximum number of the interfaces 11
is just the number of physical interfaces within the O-RU.  12
The role of interfaces shall be detected by topology discovery procedure described in subsection 14.5.2. 13
If the O-RU has any interfaces to south-node and if they are utilized for shared cell scenario, the NETCONF client shall 14
configure the higher layer ietf-interface (type =l2vlan) including configuring the corresponding mac-address and C/U-15
plane vlan-id configuration for each ietf-interface (type = ethernetCsmacd) to south-node, in addition to the higher 16
layer ietf-interface (type = l2vlan) configured for the ietf-interface (type =ethernetCsmacd) to north-node in section 4.3.  17
If an interface to a south-node is not used for shared cell scenario, the NETCONF client doesn’t need to configure the 18
higher layer ietf-interface (type = l2vlan) for it. 19
Capability of O-RU with Copy and Combine function 20
The configuration for Copy and Combine function is defined in the o-ran-shared-cell.yang module. The presence of this 21
yang module signalled in O-RU’s YANG library indicates that O-RU can support the copy and combine function. The 22
shared-cell-module-cap container includes the information for the internal maximum processing delay for both the 23
copy function and the combine function required for delay management operations. The shared-cell-module-cap 24
container also includes the information defining the maximum numbers of copy and combine functions supported. This 25
information is used by the NETCONF client to determine how many south-nodes can be supported and how many eaxc-26
ids can be used for copy and combine procedures. It also contains the information defining the compression capability 27
supported by the FHM. 28
For the cascade mode, the cascade O-RU shall support normal O-RU operations, i.e., radio transmission and reception. 29
For the FHM mode, the FHM doesn't have the capability for radio transmission and reception. The o-ran-shared-30

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
cell.yang module defines the feature FHM to indicate that O-RU acts as FHM and doesn’t have the capability of radio 1
transmission and reception. 2

14.5.2 Topology Discovery procedure 13
The O-DU shall determine the topology (adjacency relationships) of O-RUs for the shared cell. In this version of the 14
specification, only Ethernet based transport of C/U sessions for shared cells is supported. The shared cell topology 15
discovery procedure operates at the Ethernet layer, using the LBM/LBR connectivity checking procedure defined in 16
sub-section 4.6 to fill the Ethernet Forwarding Information Base (FIB), and is based on the O-DU recovering the FIB. 17
The transparent bridge functionality is used in the shared cell capable O-RUs operating in FHM and/or cascade mode. 18
In a typical operation, an O-DU performs a two-stage procedure for determining the topology: 19
I. In a first stage, the O-DU performs Ethernet connectivity monitoring on all discovered O-RU MAC addresses, 20
using the procedures defined in sub-section 4.6.1. The sending of the Ethernet loopback responses from the 21
discovered MAC addresses ensures that the transparent bridges in the O-RUs operating in FHM and cascade 22
mode will automatically learn the MAC addresses switched through these devices.  23
Note: In addition to Ethernet connectivity monitoring, DHCP discovery, call home and M-plane connection 24
establishment can be also be used to populate information in the FIB and so may be sufficient when an O-RU 25
only has a single port configured for interfacing to its north-node. 26
II. In a second stage, the O-DU uses the o-ran-ethernet-forwarding.yang module to discover which MAC 27
addresses have been learnt by the Ethernet bridge functionality. The O-DU uses the individual Ethernet 28
forwarding table entries to determine the adjacency relationships. 29
 30
The following figure illustrates an example of the MAC address configuration for a set of O-RUs configured in cascade 31
mode and FHM mode of operations, together with the associated Transparent Bridge FIB tables. 32

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        143
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
 1
Figure 76: Bridge FIB table entries learned from LBM/LMR connectivity check procedures 2
14.5.3 Shared Cell Configuration 3
Shared cell configuration consists of shared cell copy entities and shared cell combine entities. For the shared cell 4
configuration, the choice-case statement shared-cell-copy-combine-model is used for future enhancement.  5
Both shared cell copy entities and shared cell combine entities define the transport-flows for the processing elements of 6
the interface to north-node and the interface to south -node. The combine entities contain the  ta3-prime-max to be used 7
in delay management as described in sub-section 14.4.  8
As per conventional o -ran-processing-element.yang, the transport-flow (eth-flow) of the processing element is a 9
combination of o-du-mac-address, ru-mac-address and vlan-id for legacy eth-flow.  10

UL U-plane traffic only in each transport interface to south-node. When operating with COMMON shared cell copy and 1
combine mode, all U -plane traffic received from the south -node(s) is combined and forwarded to the north -node. It is 2
assumed that common compression mechanism for uplink is configured by M -plane for all O -RUs in one sha red cell 3
network. 4
When operating with SELECTIVE or SELCTIVE-BEAM-ID shared cell copy and combine mode, some selected C/U-5
plane traffic received from the north-node are copied and forwarded to the south-node and some selected U-plane traffic 6
received from south -node are combined and forwarded to the north -node. This version of the specification supports 7
SELECTIVE-BEAM-ID. SELECTIVE will be supported in a future version. 8
14.5.4 U-plane Configuration for FHM mode 9
For the FHM mode, O-RU (FHM) doesn’t need to have u-plane configuration defined in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang module. 10
Instead, O-RU (FHM) needs to have s hared-cell specific u-plane configuration. The shared-cell-copy-uplane-config is 11
the eaxc-id list used by DL C-plane, DL U-plane and UL C-plane traffic. It also contains downlink-radio-frame-offset 12
and downlink-sfn-offset to define the downlink timing of t =0 for the reception window. The shared-cell-combine-13
uplane-config is the compression method of the UL U-plane traffic applied to O-RUs within the shared cell network in 14
shared cell combine function. The compression method is configurable per eaxc-id. It a lso contains downlink-radio-15
frame-offset, downlink-sfn-offset and n-ta-offset to define the uplink timing of t=0 for the configured ta3-prime-max. 16
In addition, number-of-prb is also contained for the case that all PRBs in numPrbc are controlled by C-plane message. 17
FHM may have multiple sets of shared cell networks as described in the Figure 78 E.g., O-RU#2a and O-RU#2b are one 18
shared cell network. O -RU#2x and O -RU#2y are  another shared cell network. These two shared cell network s are 19
separated transport layer level definitions using separate processing -element/transport-flows. Nevertheless, the O -RU 20
Controller shall ensure that the eaxc -id allocation for the shared cell networks shall be unique per link (downlink or 21
uplink) in one O-RU (FHM). NETCONF client ( O-RU Controller) shall ensure to allocate unique eaxc -id for O-RU(s) 22
per link within the shared cell network(s) in one O-RU (FHM). 23
Note: shared-cell-copy-uplane-config and shared-cell-combine-uplane-config are not applicable to the cascade mode. 24
Instead, o-ran-uplane-conf.yang module is applied. 25
Note: if the FHM supports the C/U-plane monitoring timer described in section 4.10, then depending on how long the O-26
DU takes to initiate sending of C/U plane data flows, it may be advisable for the NETCONF client to initially disable the 27
operation of the timer for the FHM before carrier activation to O-RUs that are south-nodes for the FHM. Such an approach 28
will avoid the FHM sending spurious alarm notifications triggered by O -DU delays i n initializing the sending of C/U 29
plane data that exceed the default timer value. Once C/U plane data flows have commenced, the NETCONF client can 30
re-configure the timer with the desired value and hence activate monitoring of the C/U plane connectivity by the FHM. 31
14.5.5 Support of Selective Transmission and Reception Function 32
This section describes M -Plane support for selective transmission and reception function which is specified in chapter 33
11.2.1 of [2]. There are two things to be introduced for supporting the function from M-Plane perspective; 34
• Feature which indicates FHM support for selective transmission and reception function 35
• Configuration parameters which indicate the mapping information between global beamId, O-RU(s) and O-RU 36
local beamId. 37
If FHM indicates the feature “SELECTIVE-BEAM-ID” to O-DU, O-DU can configure the mapping information between 38
global beamId, O-RU(s) and O-RU local beamId to the FHM to use selective transmission and reception function. For 39
configuring the information, mapping-table-for-selective-beam-id is used. 40
14.6 Cascade-FHM mode 41
The introduction of Cascade -FHM mode is described in chapter 11.5 of [2]. This section describes mainly shared cell 42
configuration on cascaded FHMs. For other common parts, like startup procedures, topology discovery procedure etc., 43
please refer to relevant parts in chapter 14. In this version of the specification, the maximum level of cascaded FHMs is 44
limited to 2. The first cascade FHM nearest to O-DU is named FHM#1, the second FHM is named FHM#2. 45

- In DL or UL direction, existing only one south node which connects to FHM#2 and other steps are no difference 30

Chapter 15 Configured Subscriptions 5
15.1 Introduction 6
The support by an O -RU of configured subscriptions is an optional capability, advertised by the O -RU indicating it 7
supports the ietf-subscribed-notifications YANG model [37] in its YANG library together with the configured feature. 8
This capability enables an O -RU Controller to i nstall a subscription via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. 9
Importantly, the lifetime of such a configured subscription is not limited to the lifetime of the NETCONF session used to 10
establish it, enabling a configured subscription to persist even when  an O-RU has been temporarily disconnected from 11
the network.  12
The ietf-subscribed-notifications YANG model defines a transport agnostic mechanism for subscribing to and receiving 13
content from an event stream in an O-RU. An O-RU that supports configured subscriptions shall also support the encode-14
json feature together with the augmentation of the ietf-subscribed-notifications YANG model by the o-ran-ves-15
subscribed-notifications YANG model.  16
15.2 Description 17
An O-RU controller discovers the event-streams supported by an O-RU. The O-RU Controller then establishes a 18
configured subscription to a particular event-stream.  19
Note, the same NACM privileges defined in Sub-section 3.4 shall also be used by the O-RU in determining 20
whether an O-RU controller has privileges to establish a configured subscription to a particular event-stream. 21
Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends asynchronous notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-22
Collector. This capability can be used with any existing YANG notification, e.g., defined in YANG models published 23
by the O-RAN Alliance or imported from other organizations.   24

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        150
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
15.3 Procedure 1
 2
Figure 80:Message sequence exchange for provisioning a configured notification 3
Pre-condition: A NETCONF sessions is established between the O-RU and an O-RU Controller. 4
 5
1. The O-RU controller gets the streams container and discovers the event-streams supported by an O-RU 6
2. The O-RU controller uses the “establish-subscription” RPC to configure a subscription to an event-7
stream. The RPC includes the receiver container augmented with the notification-recipient schema 8
node that encodes the URI of the Event-Collector. 9
3. If the O-RU controller has the correct privileges, the O-RU accepts the configured subscription 10
4. As the lifetime of the configured subscription is not limited by the lifetime of the NETCONF session, 11
the O-RU controller can terminate the NETCONF session without causing the subscription to be 12
suspended. 13
5. After a subscription is successfully established, the O-RU immediately sends a "subscription-started" 14
notification to the Event-Collector, according to RFC8639 [37] clause 2.5. 15
6. Upon an event that triggers a YANG notification, the O-RU sends a notification over HTTPS , 16
according to RFC8639 clause 2.5. 17
 18
Post-condition: The Event-Collector is able to update its operational-state datastore with the information received in the 19
notification. 20

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        151
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
15.4 Notification Encoding  1
The O-RU shall support JSON encoding as specified in RFC 7951 [38]. An example notification object generated using 2
the o-ran-file-management.yang model and encoded following RFC 7951 is illustrated in Figure 81. 3
 4
Figure 81:Example of a JSON encoded YANG Notification 5
 6
15.5 Notification Transport 7
As described in RFC8639 clause 2.5.7, an O-RU supporting configured subscriptions must provide a YANG data model 8
capturing the necessary transport-specific configuration parameters. O-RAN compliant Event-Producers shall support 9
the o-ran-ves-subscribed-notifications YANG model.  10
For transport, the notification JSON objects encoded according to sub-section 15.4 are further encapsulated in VES 11
events. In order to enable the notifications sent to the Event-Collector to retain their native notification format/schema 12
as defined in O-RAN, IETF and other YANG models, the ONAP/VES header is used to enable the decoupling of the 13
notification payload from the overall VES event format, as illustrated in Figure 81.  14
The VES common header shall include the following fields: 15
- The value of the eventName field shall be set to “ORU-YANG/<model-identifier>:<notification-identifier>” 16
- The value of the eventID field shall be set to “stndDefined-ORU-YANG-nnnnnnnnn", where nnnnnnnnnn 17
represents the integer key for the event 18
- The value of the sourceName and reportingEntityName fields shall both be set to the value of the ru-instance-19
id leaf defined in the o-ran-operations YANG model.  20
{ "ietf-restconf:notification": {
    "eventTime": "2020-11-11T20:20:00Z",
    "o-ran-file-management:file-upload-notification": {
      "local-logical-file-path": "/O-
RAN/PM/C201805181300+0900_201805181330+0900_ABC0123456.csv",
      "remote-file-path": "/home/pm/
C201805181300+0900_201805181330+0900_ABC0123456.csv",
      "status": "SUCCESS"
    }
  }
}

15.6 Monitoring the Communications Channel between O-RU and 7
Event-Collector 8
An O-RU controller can use the NETCONF monitoring capability described in sub-section 3.6 to trigger the repeated 9
sending of a supervision-notification by the O-RU to a subscribed O-RU Controller to ensure the channel is 10
operational and able to transport asynchronous notifications using NETCONF. An equivalent capability is required to 11
be supported by those O-RUs that support configured subscriptions transported using JSON/HTTPS, to enable the 12
monitoring of the communications channel from the O-RU to the Event-Collector. The format of the heartbeat 13
notifications is identical to the Event-Collector Notification Format determined for the operation of pnfRegistration as 14

15.6.1 Heartbeat Encoding 3

 8
Figure 84:Example of a JSON encoded VES Event Carrying a Heartbeat Notification 9
15.6.2 Heartbeat Control 10
Control of the heartbeat does not use the configured subscriptions capability. An O-RU controller configures heartbeat 11
operation using the o-ran-supervision YANG model. An O-RU Controller shall configure the heartbeat-recipient-id to 12
the address(es) of the Heartbeat Event-Collector and optionally configure the heartbeat-interval leaf to a non-default 13
heartbeat interval. In order to terminate operation of the monitoring the communications channel between O-RU and the 14
Event-Collector, the O-RU shall delete the configuration in the event-collector-monitoring container. 15

when monitoring of NETCONF connectivity fails, there is no equivalent O -RU functionality defined if an O -RU 5
determines that monitoring of the communications channel between O-RU and event-collector fails, e.g., if the O-RU is 6
unable to establish a TLS connection to the event-collector.  7
Operation of the SMO when it determines that the monitoring of the communications channel between an O -RU and 8
event-collector fails is out of scope of this specification. 9

Annex A Alarm definition 1
This section contains example alarms which may be reported. 2
Obviously, alarms that are not applicable in given HW design or SW configuration shall not be reported. For example, 3
alarms related to fan monitoring are applicable to HW variants with fans. 4
In many cases alarm detection method is HW specific. It is assumed that alarm detection method is reliable to avoid 5
undetected alarms and false alarms. It is also expected that the NETCONF Server is applying mechanisms to avoid 6
unreasonably fast toggling of alarms’ state. 7
 8
The example alarms table has following columns: 9
Fault id – Numerical identifier of alarm. This ID shall be used in <alarm-notif> message (fault-id parameter). 10
Name – Name of the alarm. 11
Meaning – Description of alarm, describes high level meaning of the alarm. 12
Start condition – Defines conditions which must be fulfilled to generate alarm. If filtering time is needed, then it must be 13
defined in this column. 14
Cancel condition – Defines conditions which must be fulfilled to cancel alarm. If filtering time is needed, then it must be 15
defined in this column. 16
NETCONF Server actions on detection – Defines actions of the NETCONF Server after alarm has been detected. 17
NETCONF Server actions on cancel – Defines actions of NETCONF Server after alarm has been cancelled. 18
System recovery actions – Describes gNB level recovery actions of the NETCONF Client after alarm has been indicated 19
by NETCONF Server. This field is informative only; actions taken by the NETCONF Client are not restricted nor defined 20
in this document. System recovery action “Reset” refers to NETCONF Client forcing reset of O-RU. 21
Source – Defines possible sources of the alarm (alarm is within O-RU). The following are XML encoding provides 22
examples of the component names defined in various YANG modules that may be alarm sources inside the O-RU. 23
- < hardware xmlns= "urn:o-ran:hardware:1.0"><component><o-ran-name/></component></hardware> 24
- <fan-tray xmlns= "urn:o-ran:fan:1.0"><fan-state><name/></fan-state></fan-tray> 25
- <sync xmlns= "urn:o-ran:sync:1.0"><gnss-state><name/></gnss-state></sync> 26
- <external-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:externalio:1.0”><input><name/></input></external-io> 27
- <external-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:externalio:1.0”><output><name/></output></external-io> 28
- <ald-ports-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:ald-port:1.0”><ald-port><name/></ald-port></ald-ports-io> 29
- <port-transceivers xmlns= "urn:o-ran:transceiver:1.0”><port-transceiver-data><name/></ port-30
transceiver-data ></port-transceivers> 31
- <interfaces xmlns= "urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:yang:ietf-32
interfaces”><interface><name/></interface></interfaces> 33
- <processing-elements xmlns= "urn:o-ran:processing-element.1.0”><ru-elements><name/></ru-34
elements></processing-elements> 35
- <-ran-uplane-conf xmlns= "urn:o-ran:uplane-conf.1.0”><low-level-tx-links><name/></low-level-tx-links></ 36
o-ran-uplane-conf> 37
- <o-ran-uplane-conf xmlns= "urn:o-ran:uplane-conf.1.0”><low-level-rx-links><name/></low-level-rx-38
links></o-ran-uplane-conf> 39
 40
Note: If Source will not fit to any of above, or is empty, it means that external device (like Antenna Line Devices) cause 41
an alarm (fault is out of the O-RU). Then additional text in alarm notification is needed to clearly say what may be possible 42
fault source. 43
 44
Severity – Defines severity of the alarm [30]. 45
Critical – sub unit for which alarm has been generated is not working and cannot be used. 46

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        156
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
Major – sub unit for which alarm has been generated is degraded, it can be used but performance might be degraded. 1
Minor – sub unit for which alarm has been generated is still working. 2

B.1.1 Statistics Calculation 3
When configured by the NETCONF client, the O-RU captures value of monitored parameters. Then the O-RU calculates 4
x = f(s), where f(s) is a function selected for specific statistics instance. The function f(s) can be one of the following:  5
• f(s) = s  6
• f(s) = LOG10(s),  7
where LOG10(s) is logarithm with base 10. To avoid issues with infinity, the O-RU assumes that for s < 10 -128 value of 8
LOG10(s) is -128. 9
 10
The value of x = f(s) is applied to first, latest, min and max values; related timestamps are also updated; frequency table 11
is updated as described in the following section. 12
 13
When local measurement interval, which is not same as transceiver-measurement-interval of the measurement-object, 14
passes the O-RU captures value of a monitored parameter (s). Then the O-RU calculates x = f(s), where f is a function 15
selected for specific parameter.  The local measurement in terval is up to the O-RU implementation matter and typically 16
around 10 sec – 60 sec at earliest. 17
  18
The value of x = f(s) is applied to latest value; related timestamp is updated.   19
The O-RU updates statistics:  20
• If x < min value then x is applied to min value and related timestamp is updated.  21
• If x > max value then x is applied to max value and related timestamp is updated.  22
• Value of x is used to update frequency table as described in section Frequency Table below.  23
 24
After updates O-RU waits another interval to elapse. 25
B.1.2 Frequency Table Generation  26
Let n = bin-count, a = lower-bound, b = upper-bound, x = f(s) where s is va lue of monitored parameter and f is a 27
function selected for statistics via parameter function.   28
 29
• If n = 0 then frequency table is empty and is not updated.   30
• If n > 0 there are n bins: hk where k = 0...n-1. Initial value of each bin is zero (hk = 0 for k = 0...n-1).  31
• If x < a then bin h0 is incremented.   32

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        164
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v06.00
• If b ≤ x and n > 1 then bin hn-1 is incremented.  1
• If a ≤ x and x < b and n > 2 then bin hk is incremented for k such that   2
• k-1 ≤ (n-2) * (x-a) / (b-a) < k.  3
 4
Note value of bin should saturate at maximum without overflowing (the value is not incremented above 232-1).  5
Equivalently:  6
 7
• For k = 0, hk is a number of values x such that x < a. 8
• For k = 1 ... n-2, hk is a number of values x such that  9
• a + (b-a) * (k-1) / (n-2) ≤ x < a + (b-a) * (k) / (n-2).   10
• For k = n-1, hk is a number of values x such that b ≤ x.   11
 12
Example:   13
 14
function = LOG10, bin-count = 14, lower-bound = -12, upper-bound = 0 15
 16
• parameter value s = 0, x = f(0) = -128, -128 < -12 = a
  h0 is incremented   17
• parameter value s = 1e-12, x = f(1e-12) = -12, (14-2)*(-12-(-12))/(0-(-12)) = 12*0/12 < 1
  h1 is incremented   18
• parameter value s = 9.99e -12, x = f(9.99e -12) = -11.0004, (14-2)*(-11.0004-(-12))/(0-(-12)) = 12*0.9996/12 < 1 19
 h1 is incremented  20
• parameter value s = 1e-1, x = f(1e-1) = -1, (14-2)*(-1-(-12))/(0-(-12)) = 12*11/12 < 12
  h12 is incremented  21
• parameter value s = 1, x = f(1) = 0, 0 ≥ 0 = b
  h13 is incremented  22
 23

measurement-object Description

Annex D YANG Module Graphical Representation 1
The different released version of the set of YANG modules for the O-RU can be downloaded from O-RAN’s website 2
http://www.o-ran.org/specifications/ . The YANG models are available in a zip file, whose name is used to represent the 3
version of the YANG model and follows the numerical format defined in subsection 1.1 with the periods replaced with 4
“-”, i.e., YANG models for release 1.0.0 of the M -Plane specification are available in the file 1 -0-0.zip. This zip file 5
includes all published revisions of the YANG models supporting a particular release of the M-Plane specification. 6
This Annex provides a set of “tree -views” of the modules to provide a simplified graphical representation of the data 7
models. These trees have been automatically generated using the pyang YANG validator tool. If there are any 8
inconsistencies between the tree representation in this Annex and the yang models, the yang models shall take precedence. 9
D.1 System Folder 10
D.1.1 o-ran-supervision.yang Module 11
The format for the supervision module is provided below. 12
module: o-ran-supervision 13
  +--rw supervision 14
  +--rw cu-plane-monitoring! 15
     |  +--rw configured-cu-monitoring-interval?   uint8 16
     +--rw event-collector-monitoring {or-feat:NON-PERSISTENT-MPLANE}? 17
        +--rw heartbeat-interval?       uint8 18
        +--rw heartbeat-recipient-id*   event-collector-id 19
  rpcs: 20
    +---x supervision-watchdog-reset 21
       +---w input 22
       |  +---w supervision-notification-interval?   uint16 23
       |  +---w guard-timer-overhead?                uint16 24
       +--ro output 25
          +--ro next-update-at?   yang:date-and-time 26
          +--ro error-message?    string 27
 28
  notifications: 29
    +---n supervision-notification 30

module: o-ran-usermgmt 33
  +--rw users 34
     +--rw user* [name] 35
        +--rw name            nacm:user-name-type 36
        +--rw account-type?   enumeration 37
        +--rw password?       password-type 38
        +--rw enabled?        boolean 39
 40
  rpcs: 41
    +---x chg-password 42
       +---w input 43
       |  +---w currentPassword       password-type 44
       |  +---w newPassword           password-type 45
       |  +---w newPasswordConfirm    password-type 46
       +--ro output 47
          +--ro status            enumeration 48
          +--ro status-message?   string 49

entity that downloads, uses or otherwise accesses any O-RAN Specification, including its Affiliates (the “Adopter”). 5

Section 1: DEFINITIONS 7
1.1 “Affiliate” means an entity that directly or indirectly controls, is controlled by, or is under common control with 8
another entity, so long as such control exists. For the purpose of this Section, “Control” means beneficial ownership of 9
fifty (50%) percent or more of the voting stock or equity in an entity. 10
1.2 “Compliant Implementation” means any system, device, method or operation (whether implemented in hardware, 11
software or combinations thereof) that fully conforms to a Final Specification. 12
1.3 “Adopter(s)” means all entities, who are not Members, Contributors or Academic Contributors, including their 13
Affiliates, who wish to download, use or otherwise access O-RAN Specifications. 14
1.4 “Minor Update” means an update or revision to an O-RAN Specification published by O-RAN Alliance that does 15
not add any significant new features or functionality and remains interoperable with the prior version of an O-RAN 16
Specification. The term “O-RAN Specifications” includes Minor Updates. 17
1.5 “Necessary Claims” means those claims of all present and future patents and patent applications, other than design 18
patents and design registrations, throughout the world, which (i) are owned or otherwise licensable by a Member, 19
Contributor or Academic Contributor during the term of its Member, Contributor or Academic Contributorship; (ii) 20
such Member, Contributor or Academic Contributor has the right to grant a license without the payment of 21
consideration to a third party; and (iii) are necessarily infringed by a Compliant Implementation (without considering 22
any Contributions not included in the Final Specification). A claim is necessarily infringed only when it is not possible 23
on technical (but not commercial) grounds, taking into account normal technical practice and the state of the art 24
generally available at the date any Final Specification was published by the O-RAN Alliance or the date the patent 25
claim first came into existence, whichever last occurred, to make, sell, lease, otherwise dispose of, repair, use or operate 26
a Compliant Implementation without infringing that claim. For the avoidance of doubt in exceptional cases where a 27
Final Specification can only be implemented by technical solutions, all of which infringe patent claims, all such patent 28
claims shall be considered Necessary Claims. 29
1.6 “Defensive Suspension” means for the purposes of any license grant pursuant to Section 3, Member, Contributor, 30
Academic Contributor, Adopter, or any of their Affiliates, may have the discretion to include in their license a term 31
allowing the licensor to suspend the license against a licensee who brings a patent infringement suit against the 32
licensing Member, Contributor, Academic Contributor, Adopter, or any of their Affiliates. 33
